Absolute Ibra' Despite Condition of Payment
Ruling on ibra' conditioned on future payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ibra' conditioned on future payment and distinguish between cases based on wording order.

Core Idea
If the ibra' is mentioned first, it remains absolute even if a condition follows.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario from the Hanafi fiqh of ibra' (debt remission). In the third scenario discussed, a creditor discharges half a debt on condition that the debtor pays the remaining half by a certain date. The ruling hinges on the order of phrases: whether the ibra' or the payment is mentioned first. Understanding this distinction clarifies the Hanafi approach to conditional legal acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and condition
What is the ibra' and what condition is attached? Here, the creditor discharges 500 of a 1000 debt on condition the debtor pays 500 tomorrow.
The ibra' is for part of the debt, not the whole.
2
Determine the sequence of phrases
Which came first: the ibra' statement or the condition? In this scenario, the ibra' is stated first, then the condition.
Order matters in Hanafi law.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
Absolute ibra' once established is not removed by subsequent doubt. Payment cannot be a valid consideration (iwad) because it is already obligatory, but it can be a condition. The preceding absolute ibra' persists.
Doubt does not remove what is established.
4
Contrast with the alternative sequence
If the payment is mentioned first, the ibra' becomes conditional because the ibra' is associated with the payment from the start.
This is the first scenario mentioned in the text.
5
State the ruling
In this third scenario, the ibra' is valid and unconditional. The debt of 500 is discharged whether the debtor pays or not.
The remaining 500 is still due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله والثالث اذا قال .... الخ - تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ اس نے ہزار میں سے پانچ سو سے اس شرط پر بری کیا کہ کل کے روز پانچ سو دیدے کے اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ ابراء ہو گیا خواہ وہ پانچ سودے یا نہ دے۔ اس لئے کہ اس نے اولا ابراء کو مطلق رکھا ہے تو مطلق ابراء حاصل ہوا۔ پھر اس نے پانچ سو کی ادائیگی کو اداء کو عوض بنایا ہے۔ حالانکہ اداء اس لائق نہیں کہ وہ عوض مطلق ہو اسلئے کہ عوض تو وہ ہے جو ابھی حاصل نہ ہو اور یہاں پانچ سو کی ادائیگی حاصل ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ ابراء بعض کے بغیر بھی مقروض کے ذمہ واجب ہے۔ البتہ ادائیگی شرط ہونے کے لائق ہے تو اب یہ شک پڑ گیا کہ اس نے ابراء کو شرط کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے یا نہیں۔ پس جو مطلق ابراء اولا حاصل ہو چکا وہ اس شک سے زائل نہ ہوگا۔ لہذا ابراء کو مقید نہیں کیا جائے گا بخلاف اس صورت کے جب اس نے پانچ سو کی ادائیگی کو پہلے بیان کیا (جیسا کہ پہلی صورت میں ہے ) کہ اس میں ابراء مقید ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ابراء اداء کے ساتھ مقرون ہے۔ تو اس لحاظ سے کہ وہ عوض ہونے کے لائق نہیں ابراء مطلق واقع ہو گا اور اس لحاظ سے کہ وہ شرط ہونے کے لائق ہے ابراء مطلق نہ ہوگا بہر حال شک کی وجہ سے اطلاق ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ پس بدائت بالا براہ اور اور بدات باداء الخمس ماتہ دونوں میں فرق ظاہر ہو گیا ( یہی وہ فرق ہے جس کا وعدہ سابق میں کیا تھا)۔
The third scenario: He discharges him from five hundred out of a thousand on condition that he gives him five hundred tomorrow. The ruling is that the ibra' takes place whether he gives the five hundred or not. Because he first made the ibra' absolute, so absolute ibra' occurred. Then he made the payment of five hundred a consideration (iwad), but payment is not fit to be a consideration because consideration is something not yet obtained, whereas here the payment of five hundred is already obligatory on the debtor (even without ibra' of part). However, payment can be a condition. So there is doubt whether he conditioned the ibra' or not. The absolute ibra' that first occurred is not removed by this doubt. Therefore, the ibra' is not made conditional. This differs from the case where he mentioned the payment of five hundred first (as in the first scenario), where the ibra' becomes conditional because the ibra' is associated with the payment. So from the perspective that it is not fit as consideration, the ibra' is absolute; from the perspective that it is fit as a condition, the ibra' is not absolute. Nevertheless, due to doubt, absoluteness is not established. Thus a distinction appears between ibra' preceded by ibra' and ibra' preceded by payment of five hundred.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage presents the third scenario from the Hidayah commentary. It is a ruling statement regarding a discharge (ibra') conditioned on future payment. The author explains that if a creditor says 'I discharge you from 500 out of 1000 on condition that you pay me 500 tomorrow,' the ibra' is valid and the debt is discharged regardless of whether the debtor pays tomorrow. The reasoning is that the ibra' was expressed first in an absolute manner, and the subsequent mention of payment as a condition does not negate the absolute ibra'. Payment cannot be a valid consideration (iwad) because it is already obligatory, so it cannot be an exchange. However, it could be a condition, but that creates doubt. Since absoluteness preceded, doubt does not remove it. This contrasts with the first scenario where the payment was mentioned first and the ibra' followed, making it conditional. The key distinction is the order of words: if the payment is mentioned first, the ibra' is conditional; if the ibra' is mentioned first, it remains absolute.

Key Terms
ابراء (ibra'): A discharge or remission of a debt, releasing the debtor from obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The ibra' is invalid and the full debt remains.
B) The ibra' is valid and the debt of 1000 is reduced to 500.
C) The ibra' is valid and the entire 1000 is discharged.
D) The creditor can revoke the ibra'.

Key Takeaway
The sequence of wording in an ibra' determines whether a subsequent condition binds; if ibra' is first, it remains absolute.

Absolute Ibra' Without Specified Time
Ibra' without time specification is absolute and valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for an ibra' that does not specify a time for payment and explain why it is considered absolute.

Core Idea
Ibra' without a time condition is absolute and immediately discharges the debt.

In this lesson we examine a specific scenario from the Hidayah: a creditor says 'Pay me 500 dirhams and you are free from the rest' without mentioning when the payment must occur. The Hanafi school rules that this ibra' is valid and absolute—meaning the remaining debt is forgiven immediately. The reasoning hinges on the fact that the debtor is already obligated to pay at some time, so the specification of payment cannot serve as a valid condition or consideration. This contrasts with cases where a specific time is named, which could make the ibra' conditional.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The creditor states: 'Pay me 500 dirhams and you are free from the rest.' No time for payment is mentioned. Note that this is a conditional phrase but without a temporal specification.
The wording uses 'on condition that' but the time is absent.
2
Determine the Ruling
According to the Hanafi school, the ibra' is valid (sahih) and the remaining debt is discharged immediately. The creditor cannot later revoke it.
The ruling is found in the Hidayah commentary.
3
Trace the Legal Reasoning
The reason is that payment 'at some time' is already obligatory on the debtor; therefore, requiring payment cannot be a real condition or a consideration (since it is not a new obligation). Hence the ibra' becomes absolute (mutlaq).
If payment were a valid condition, the ibra' would be conditional, but here it is not.
4
Contrast with a Specified Time
If the creditor had said 'Pay me tomorrow and you are free', the ibra' would be conditional because a specific time gives a valid purpose (gharaz) that the debtor must fulfill.
This contrast highlights the importance of time specification in determining the nature of ibra'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و الرابع اذا قال .... الخ - چوتھی صورت یہ ہے کہ اس نے ادائیگی کا وقت ذکر کئے بغیر یوں کہا۔ کہ تو مجھے پانچ سو در ہم اس شرط پرادا کر کرہ تو باقی سے بری ہے۔ اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ ابرا صحیح ہے اور قرضہ نہیں لوٹے گا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ ابراء مطلق ہے۔ کیونکہ جب اس نے اداء کا کوئی وقت بیان نہیں کیا تو اداء کوئی صحیح غرض نہ ہوئی۔ اس لئے کہ کسی نہ کسی وقت دادا کرنا تو خود مقروض پر واجب ہے۔ پس پانچ سو کی ادائیگی شرط کے معنی میں نہیں ہو سکتی یہاں تک کہ اس سے تقیید حاصل ہو اور معاوضہ پر اس لئے محمول نہیں کر سکتے کہ وہ عوض ہونے کے قابل نہیں۔ جب دونوں باتیں متعذر ہیں تو ابراء لا محالہ مطلق ہو گا۔ بخلاف اس کے جب اداء کا کوئی وقت بیان کر دے کہ اس صورت میں ابراء مقید ہو سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ کل کے دن ادا کرنے میں غرض صحیح متعلق ہے
The fourth scenario: He says without mentioning a time for payment: 'You give me five hundred dirhams on condition that you are free from the rest.' The ruling is that the ibra' is valid and the debt is not returned. The reason is that this ibra' is absolute. Because when he did not specify a time for payment, the payment is not a valid purpose (gharaz), since paying at some time is already obligatory on the debtor. So the payment of five hundred cannot be a condition to achieve restriction, nor can it be considered as consideration because it is not fit for being a consideration. When both possibilities are hindered, the ibra' necessarily becomes absolute. Unlike the case where he specifies a time for payment, as in that case the ibra' can be conditional because specifying tomorrow for payment contains a valid purpose.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth scenario from the Hidayah commentary. It is a ruling statement regarding an ibra' where the creditor says 'Pay me 500 and you are free from the rest' without specifying when. The author rules that such an ibra' is valid and absolute, meaning the discharge is effective immediately and the remaining debt is forgiven. The reasoning is that without a specified time, the payment cannot serve as a valid condition or consideration because payment is already obligatory. Therefore the ibra' is unconditional. This contrasts with the case where a specific time is mentioned, which could make the ibra' conditional. The key is that the creditor's statement is interpreted as an absolute discharge.

Key Terms
ابراء مطلق (ibra' mutlaq): An absolute discharge without any condition or time limitation.
ابراء مقید (ibra' muqayyad): A conditional discharge that depends on a specific event, such as payment by a certain time.
غرض صحیح (gharaz sahih): A valid purpose or benefit that justifies a condition in a contract or discharge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the debtor paid the 500 dirhams immediately.
B) Because the creditor did not specify a time for payment.
C) Because the creditor used the word 'on condition'.
D) Because the amount paid (500) equals the remaining debt.

Key Takeaway
An ibra' without a specified time is absolute and discharges the debt upon utterance, regardless of when payment occurs.

Invalidity of Explicitly Conditional Ibra'
Ibra' suspended on a condition is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ibra' suspended on an explicit condition and explain the reason based on the dual nature of ibra' (isqat and tamlik).

Core Idea
Explicit condition invalidates ibra' because tamlik cannot be conditional, overriding isqat's validity.

In this passage, the fifth scenario from the Hidayah commentary is presented: an ibra' (discharge from debt) that is explicitly tied to a condition – using words like 'if' or 'when' – is invalid. The ruling hinges on the dual legal nature of ibra': it is both an isqat (dropping of a right, which can be conditional) and a tamlik (transfer, which cannot). When the condition is explicit, the tamlik aspect dominates, rendering the ibra' invalid. When the condition is only implicit, the isqat aspect is considered, and the ibra' remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes an ibra' where the person explicitly states a condition using words like 'if' or 'when'. Recognize that this is the fifth scenario in the Hidayah.
Explicit condition means the condition is stated in clear terms.
2
Recognize the dual elements of ibra'
Ibra' has two legal aspects: isqat (dropping of a right) and tamlik (transfer). Isqat does not require acceptance and can be conditional; tamlik requires acceptance and cannot be conditional.
This dual nature is key to the ruling.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
Since ibra' partakes of both elements, its validity depends on the clarity of the condition. If the condition is explicit (like 'if'), the tamlik aspect overrides and invalidates the ibra'. If the condition is implicit (understood from context), the isqat aspect governs and the ibra' is valid.
The passage explicitly contrasts explicit vs. implicit conditions.
4
Note the practical consequence
This distinction determines whether a conditional discharge is legally effective. A creditor must be careful to avoid explicit conditions if they intend the ibra' to be valid.
In practice, they should make the discharge unconditional or let the understanding remain implicit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله والخامس اذا قال ... الخ - پانچویں صورت یہ ہے کہ اس نے صریح شرط بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ اگر یا جب یا مہر گاہ تو مجھے پانچ ہے اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ اسقاط ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ قبول کرنے پر موقوف نہیں ہوتا اور اس میں تملیک کے معنی بھی ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ رد کرنے سے رد ہو جاتا ہے اور تملیک بیع وغیرہ شرط کے ساتھ جائز نہیں اور اسقاط کی تعلیق عتاق و طلاق وغیرہ شرط کے ساتھ جائز ہے۔ پس ابراء جو دونوں معنوں پر مشتمل ہے اس کی بابت ہم نے کہا کہ جب شرط کی تصریح نہ ہو تو صحیح ہے اور جب شرط کی تصریح ہو تو صحیح نہیں۔ عملا بالشبهین۔
قـولـه لأنه ليس بمكره ... الخ -مکرہ نہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ وہ اقامت بینہ کے ذریعہ سے اس کو دفع کر سکتا ہے۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ یہاں ایک طرح کا اضطرار نفاذ تصرف سے مانع نہیں ہوتا۔ چنانچہ اگر کوئی شخص انتہائی بھوک سے معطر ہو کر کھانے کی چیز گراں قیمت پر خرید لے یا اپنی کوئی چیز طعام کے عوض میں فروخت کر دے تو اس کا تصرف نافذ ہوتا ہے۔ اگر چہ وہ اس کی طرف مضطر ہے۔
The fifth scenario: He explicitly states a condition by saying 'if' or 'when' or 'as long as you give me five hundred [then you are free].' The reason is that ibra' is isqat (dropping of right) such that it does not require acceptance, but it also has the meaning of tamlik (transfer) such that it is repudiated by refusal. Tamlik in sale etc. is not valid with a condition, while isqat can be suspended on a condition like manumission and divorce. So ibra', which includes both meanings, we rule that when the condition is not explicit it is valid, and when the condition is explicit it is not valid, acting on both aspects. 
His saying: 'because he is not coerced' - He is not coerced because he can repel it through testimony. The point is that a sort of duress does not prevent the validity of the transaction. For example, if someone extremely hungry buys food at a high price or sells something for food, his transaction is valid even though he is in need.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth scenario from the Hidayah commentary, followed by a note on coercion. The ruling is that an ibra' (discharge) explicitly suspended on a condition (using words like 'if' or 'when') is invalid. The reason is that ibra' has a dual nature: it is an isqat (dropping of a right) which does not require acceptance and can be suspended, and it is also a tamlik (transfer) which cannot be conditional. Since ibra' partakes of both, if the condition is explicit, the tamlik aspect dominates and makes it invalid. If the condition is implicit (as in previous scenarios), the isqat aspect is considered. The note about coercion clarifies that even if a person is in a desperate situation, his transactions are valid as long as he is not legally coerced (mukrah).

Key Terms
اسقاط (isqat): The dropping or relinquishment of a right, which does not require acceptance and can be conditional.
تملیک (tamlik): The transfer of ownership, which requires acceptance and cannot be conditional.
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspending a legal effect on a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is an ibra' with an explicit condition (e.g., 'if you pay, you are free') invalid according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because ibra' requires immediate payment.
B) Because ibra' contains elements of tamlik which cannot be conditional.
C) Because the debtor must accept the condition.
D) Because the condition is impossible to fulfill.

Key Takeaway
An explicit condition invalidates ibra' in Hanafi fiqh due to its tamlik aspect; implicit conditions are valid.

Joint Debt: Partner's Options When One Settles
Rules of joint debt when one partner settles with the debtor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on joint debt when one partner settles, identify the two options for the non-settling partner, and apply the principle of participation (musharakat) to analogous cases.

Core Idea
When one partner receives a joint debt payment, the other has the right to share in what was received, like offspring and fruit.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hidayah on joint debts. When two people are owed a debt jointly, and one partner settles his share by accepting a cloth, the other partner is given a choice: either pursue the debtor for his half or take half of the cloth. The underlying principle is that receipt perfects the value of the debt, giving rise to a right of participation (musharakat) for the non-receiving partner.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario and the ruling
Read the opening lines: when a joint debt exists, and one partner makes a sulh for his share accepting a cloth, the other partner has two options.
The key term is the non-settling partner's khiyar.
2
Grasp the principle of musharakat
The author explains that if one partner receives any part of the joint debt, the other has the right to share in what was received, because the value of the debt increases upon receipt.
The increase returns to the original right.
3
Identify the dalil (qiyas)
The increase is analogized to offspring and fruit, which are shared between co-owners. This is a qiyas on the common principle that increase from a shared right is also shared.
The specific phrase: 'فَيَصِيرُ كَزِيَادَةِ الْوَلَدِ وَالثَّمَرَةِ'.
4
Note the condition for limitation
The options are limited if the settling partner guarantees a quarter of the debt to the other. Then the non-settling partner cannot take from the received goods and must pursue the debtor.
The guarantee substitutes the right of participation.
5
Apply to a variant case
The text extends: if one partner receives half of his share, the other can participate in what was received, and then both pursue the debtor for the remainder.
This reinforces the principle of ongoing partnership in the debt.

Source Text

مشترک دین کا بیان دین دو آدمیوں میں مشترک ہو ایک نے اپنے حصہ دین کے بدلے کپڑے پر صلح کر لی تو دوسرے شریک کو اختیار ہے کہ نصف دین لے یا نصف کپڑا لے ۔ مگر جب شریک ربع دین کا ضامن بن جائے
(فصل فِي الدَيْنِ الْمُشْتَرَكِ) وَإِذَا كَانَ الدَيْنُ بَيْنَ شَرِيكَيْنِ فَصَالَحَ اَحَدُهُمَا مِنْ نَصِيبِهِ عَلَى ثَوْبِ فَشَرِيْكُهُ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَتْبَعَ الَّذِى عَلَيْهِ الدَّيْنُ بِنِصْفِهِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَ نِصْفَ التَّوْبِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَضْمَنَ لَهُ شَرِيكَهُ رَبِّعُ الدَّيْنِ وَأَصْلُ هَذَا أَنْ الدَيْـنَ الْمُشْتَرَكَ بَيْنَ اثْنَيْنِ إِذَا قَبَضَ أَحَدُهُمَا شَيْئًا مِنْهُ فَلِصَاحِبِهِ أَنْ يُشَارِكَهُ فِي الْمَقْبُوضِ لأَنَّهُ ازْدَادَ بِالْقَبْضِ إِذْ مَالِيَةُ الدَيْنِ بِاعْتِبَارِ عَاقِبَةِ الْقَبْضِ وَهَذِهِ الزِيَادَةُ رَاجِعَةٌ إِلَى أَصْلِ الْحَقِّ فَيَصِيرُ كَزِيَادَةِ الْوَلَدِ وَالثَّمَرَةِ فَلَه حَقُ الْمُشَارَكَةِ وَلَكِنَّه قَبْلَ الْمُشَارَكَةِ بَاقٍ عَلَى مِلْكِ الْقَابِضِ لِاَنَّ الْعَيْنَ غَيْرُ الدَّيْنِ حَقِيقَةً وَقَدَ قَبَضَهَ بَدَلًا عَنْ حَقِهِ فَيَمْلِكُهُ حَتَّى يَنْفُذَ تَصَرُّفَهُ فِيهِ وَيَضْمَنُ لِشَرِيكِهِ حِصَتْه وَالدَّيْنُ الْمُشْتَرَكُ أَنْ يَكُونَ وَاجِبًا بِسَبَبِ مُتَّحِدٍ كَتَمَنِ الْمَبِيعِ إِذَا كَانَ صَفَقَةً وَاحِدَةً وَثَمَنِ الْمَالِ الْمُشْتَرَكِ وَالْمَوْرُوثِ بَيْنَهُمَا وَقِيمَةُ الْمُسْتَهَلَكِ الْمُشْتَرَكِ فَإِذَا عَرَفْتَ هَذَا نَقُولُ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْكِتَابِ لَهُ أَنْ يَتَّبِعَ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْأَصْلُ لِأَنَّ نَصِيبَه بَاقٍ فِي ذِمَّتِهِ لاَنَّ الْقَابِضَ قَبَضَ نَصِيبَه لَكِنْ لَهُ حَقُّ الْمُشَارَكَةِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَ نِصْفَ التَّوْبِ لِاَنَّ لَهُ حَقَّ الْمُشَارَكَةِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَضْمَنَ لَهُ شَرِيْكُهُ رُبعَ الدَّيْنِ لِاَنَّ حَقَّهُ فِي ذلِكَ. قَالَ وَلَوِ اسْتَوْفِي أَحَدُهُمَا نِصْفَ نَصِيبِهِ مِنَ الدَيْنِ كَانَ لِشَرِيكِهِ أَنْ يُشَارِكَهُ فِيمَا قَبَضَ لِمَا قُلْنَا ثُمَّ يَرْجِعَانِ عَلَى الْغَرِيمِ بِالْبَاقِي لِأَنَّهُمَا لَمَا اشْتَرَكَا قُبُوضِ لَابُدَّ أَنْ يَبْقِ ى الشركة
Section on joint debt: When a debt is shared between two partners, and one of them makes a sulh for his share on a cloth, then his partner has the option: if he wishes he can pursue the debtor for his half, or if he wishes he can take half of the cloth, unless his partner guarantees for him a quarter of the debt. The basis of this is that if one of them receives anything of the joint debt, his partner has the right to share in what was received, because the debt increased by receipt—since the value of the debt is in regard to the outcome of receipt. And this increase returns to the original right, so it becomes like the increase of offspring and fruit. So he has the right of participation. But before participation, the received item remains in the ownership of the receiver because the physical item is different from the debt in reality, and he received it as a substitute for his right, so he owns it such that his disposal over it is effective, and he is liable to his partner for his share. A joint debt is that which is due from a single cause, like the price of sold goods when it is one transaction, or the price of jointly owned property, or inherited property, or the value of jointly consumed property. Knowing this, we say in the book's issue: He may pursue the original debtor because his share remains in his liability, since the receiver received his share, but he has the right of participation. If he wishes, he can take half of the cloth because he has the right of participation, unless his partner guarantees for him a quarter of the debt because his right lies in that. He (Imam) said: If one of them receives half of his share of the debt, his partner has the right to participate in what he received, for what we said. Then both together pursue the debtor for the remainder, because when they participated in the receipt, ownership must remain shared.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a fasl (section) from the Hidayah on joint debt (dayn mushtarak). It provides a ruling: when two partners share a debt owed by a third party, and one partner settles his share by accepting a cloth, the other partner has two options: either demand half the debt from the debtor, or take half of the cloth. However, if the first partner guarantees a quarter of the debt to the other, then the option is limited. The author then explains the underlying principle (asl): if one partner receives any part of the joint debt, the other partner has the right to share in what was received because the receipt increases the value (the debt becomes actual property). The received item is analogized to offspring and fruit, which are shared. However, before participation, the receiver owns the item fully (because it is a real asset, not the debt itself), but he is liable to his partner for his share. The passage also defines a joint debt: it must arise from a single cause, such as a single sale price or the value of jointly consumed property. Finally, it notes a variant: if one partner receives half of his share, the other can participate in it, and then both pursue the remainder from the debtor.

Key Terms
دین مشترک (dayn mushtarak): A debt that is jointly owed to two or more partners, arising from a single cause.
مشارکت (musharakat): The right of a partner to share in what the other partner has received from the common debtor.
خیار (khayar): The option given to the non-settling partner to choose between pursuing the debtor or taking part of the received goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling on joint debt, if one partner settles his share by taking a cloth, what are the options for the other partner?
A) He can only take half the cloth from his partner.
B) He can either pursue the debtor for his half of the debt or take half of the cloth.
C) He must accept half the cloth and cannot pursue the debtor.
D) He can demand the entire debt from the debtor himself.

Key Takeaway
When one partner receives payment of a joint debt, the other partner has the right to share in what was received, analogous to the sharing of offspring and fruit among co-owners.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Joint Debt Settlement: One Partner Takes Cloth
Commentary on the ruling for a partner's settlement of joint debt with cloth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options available to a non-settling partner when one partner settles a joint debt, and apply the Hanafi qiyas to determine the ruling.

Core Idea
A partner who collects early gains an advantage; the other partner can share the collected amount or pursue the debtor.

When two partners hold a joint debt and one settles his share by accepting a cloth, the other partner retains important rights. This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling, the reasoning based on qiyas to joint property, and the effect of a guarantee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Options
Read the passage to identify the core scenario: two partners share a joint debt; one settles his half by taking cloth. The non-settling partner has two options: take half the cloth or pursue the debtor for his share.
2
Understand the Legal Reasoning (Qiyas)
The passage uses qiyas to joint property: early collection yields an advantage (cash vs. future payment), like a child from a joint slave-girl. This advantage is shared. Identify the illa: the collector obtains an increase from the original right.
The illa is 'advantage from early payment' which is similar to natural increase from joint ownership.
3
Analyze the Exception Clause
If the settling partner guarantees to pay a quarter of the debt (half of the other's share), the other loses the right to take the cloth. Determine which option is removed: the option to participate in the cloth. The right to pursue the debtor remains.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists on the scope of the exception, but the mufta bihi is that it removes the participation option.
4
Apply the Principle
Consider a similar scenario: two partners jointly sell a car for deferred payment. One partner collects the full amount early. Apply the same principle: the other partner can share the collected money or claim from the buyer.
The key is whether the collecting partner gained an advantage. Early payment is always advantageous in Hanafi fiqh.

كتاب الصلح.
كے اعتبار سے ہے۔ اور یہ زیادتی اصل حق کی جانب راجع ہے تو بچہ اور پھل کی زیادتی کے مثل ہو گئی۔ پس ہر شریک کو حق مشارکت - مشارکت سے پہلے وہ ملک قابض پر باقی ہے کیونکہ عین حقیقۂ غیر دین ہے اور اس نے اپنے حق کے عوض میں لیا ہے تو وہ اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ اس میں اس کا تصرف نافذ ہوگا۔ اور اپنے شریک کے لئے اس کے حصہ کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اور مشترک قرضہ وہ ہے جو سبب متحد سے واجب ہو جیسے مبیع کا شمن جب کہ بصفقہ واحدہ ہو۔ اور جیسے مشترک یا مورث مال کا شمن اور جیسے تلف شدہ مشترک مال کی قیمت۔ جب یہ معلوم ہو گیا تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ مسئلہ کتاب میں شریک کو اختیار ہے کہ اس کا دامن گیر ہو جس پر اصل ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا حصہ بذمہ مدیون باقی ہے۔ کیونکہ قابض نے صرف اپنا حصہ وصول کر لیا ہے لیکن اس کو مشارکت کا حق ہے۔ اور چاہے آدھا کپڑا لے لے۔ کیونکہ اس کو مشارکت کا حق ہے مگر یہ کہ اس کے لئے اس کا شریک چوتھائی قرض کا ضامن ہو جائے۔ کیونکہ اس کا حق اسی میں ہے۔ اگر ان میں کوئی اپنا نصف قرضہ وصول کر چکا تو اس کا شریک مقبوض میں شریک ہوسکتا ہے۔ پھر دونوں شریک باقی مقروض سے وصول کریں اس لئے کہ جب مقبوض میں دونوں شریک ہوئے تو باقی ضرور شرکت پر ہو گا۔ تشریح قوله وَإذ كان الدين .... الخ قرضہ دو شریکوں کے درمیان مشترک ہے ان میں سے ایک شریک نے اپنے حصہ کی طرف سے کسی کپڑے پر صلح کرلی تو دوسرے شریک کو اختیار ہو گا چاہے آدھا کپڑا لے لے چاہے اصل مدیون سے اپنا حصہ طلب کرے لیکن اگر شریک مصالح اس کے لئے چو تھائی دین کا ضامن ہو جائے تو پھر دوسرے شریک کا کپڑے میں حق باقی نہ رہے گا۔
قوله الا ان يضمن له .... الخ - صاحب نہایہ اور اورشیخ اتقانی نے کہا ہے کہ یہ فشریکہ بالخياراہ سے استثناء ہے۔ صاحب نہایہ نے بھی اپنے قول فانه لاخيار لشريكه في ابتاع الغريم سے اسی کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ اور اس کو صاحب کفایہ نے احسن کہا ہے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ غیر مصالح شریک کو مذکور اختیار ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ اس کا شریک ربع دین کا ضامن ہو جائے کہ اس صورت میں اس کی اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن تقریر کافی کا ظاہر اور صاحب کفایہ کی صراحت یہ ہے کہ یہ ان شاء اخذ نصف الثوبہ سے استثناء ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جب شریک اس کے لئے ربع دین کا ضامن ہو گیا تو اب اس کو نصف ثوب میں شرکت کی ولایت نہیں رہی۔ اور یہ بھی ممکن ہے کہ ان شاء اتبع الذى عَلَيْهِ الدين بنصف سے استثناء ہو۔ اس لئے کہ جب شریک اس کے لئے نصف مقبوض کا ضامن ہو گیا تو اب اس کو نصف دین واپس لینے کی ولایت نہیں رہی۔ بل يرجع بربعہ۔ قوله واصل هذا...... الخ - صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس باب میں قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جو قرضہ دو شریکوں میں مشترک ہو اور ان میں سے ایک شریک کچھ حصہ وصول کرے تو دوسرے شریک کو اختیار ہوتا ہے چاہے وہ اس وصول کردہ حصہ میں شریک ہو جائے اور چاہے اصل مدیون سے اپنے حصہ کا مطالبہ کرے۔ وصول کردہ حصہ میں شریک ہو جانے کا اختیار اس لئے ہے کہ اس نے وصولیابی میں زیادتی لے لی۔ بایں معنی کہ نقد کو ادھار پر ایک قسم کی مزیت ہے اس لئے کہ قرض کی مالیت انجام کار وصول ہو جانے کے لحاظ سے ہے تو جس نے ابھی وصول نہیں کیا۔ اس کے حصہ میں گو یا مالیت نہیں ہے۔ اور وصول کنندہ نے بالفعل اس کی مالیت پالی۔ پس شرکت کے باوجود اس نے زیادہ پالیا اور یہ زیادتی چونکہ اصل حق کی
جانب راجع ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا۔ جیسے مشتر کہ باندی سے بچہ یا مشترک درخت سے پھل پیدا ہو کہ اس میں ہر شریک کو مشارکت کا حق ہوتا ہے۔ قوله ولكنه قبل المشاركة... الخ - یعنی ایک شریک نے جو کچھ وصول کیا ہے وہ دوسرے شریک اختیار شرکت سے پہلے وصول کنندہ ہی کی ملک پر باقی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے جو کچھ وصول کیا وہ مین ہو گیا۔ اور عین و دین میں حقیقت مغایرت ہے مگر اس نے چونکہ اس مین کو اپنے حق کے عوض میں لیا ہے اس لئے وہ اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر وصول کردہ میں اس نے ہبہ وغیرہ کا کوئی تصرف کیا تو نافذ ہوگا اور اپنے شریک کے لئے اس کے حصہ کے بقدر ضامن ہو گا۔ اسی لئے مسئلہ میں کہا ہے۔ الا ان يضمن له شريكه ربع الدين
قوله والدين المشترك... الخ - دین مشترک اس کو کہتے ہیں جو سبب متحد کے ذریعہ واجب ہو ۔ جیسے اس مبیع کا شمن جس کی بیع بصفقہ واحدہ ہوئی ہو۔ مثلاً دونوں نے اپنا اپنا غلام ملا کر ایک ہی بولی میں دو ہزار کے عوض فروخت کیا تو یہ ثمن مشترک ہو جائے گا۔ جو مشتری پر قرضہ ہے اور جیسے وہ دین جو دو آدمیوں کا موروث ہو یا عین مستهلک مشترک کی قیمت ہو۔ مثلاً ان دونوں کے مشترک مال کو کسی نے تلف کیا تو قیمت مشترکہ ہو گی۔ قوله فاذا عرفت هذا .... الخ - جب مذکوره اصول اور دین کی تعریف سامنے آگئی تو اب مسئلہ کتاب کا حکم یہ ہوگا کہ جس شریک نے صلح نہیں کی اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اصل مدیون کا دامن گیر ہو۔ کیونکہ صلح کنندہ نے صرف اپنا حصہ وصول کیا ہے۔ اس کا حصہ بذمہ مدیون باقی ہے۔ لیکن غیر مصالح کو حق مشارکت بھی ہے اور یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ چاہے نصف کپڑا لے لے جس پر صلح واقع ہوئی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو کپڑے میں بھی حق مشارکت حاصل ہے۔ لیکن اگر اس کا شریک چوتھائی قرضہ کا ضامن ہو جائے تو پھر وہ کپڑے میں سے نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ اس کا حق اصل قرضہ میں ہے۔ سوال کپڑے میں حق مشارکت نہیں ہونا چاہیئے اس لئے کہ صلح جب جنس حق کے خلاف پر ہو تو وہ معاوضہ ہوتی ہے اور معاوضہ محضہ میں شریک کے لئے کپڑے میں کوئی سبیل نہیں ہوتی۔ جواب بوسط خواہر زادہ میں ہے جنس حق کے خلاف پر صلح عام احکام میں شراء ہوتی ہے۔ اور بعض میں مین حق کا استیفاء اور معاوضہ محفہ کسی طرح بھی بعض حق کا استیفاء نہیں ہوتا۔ قوله ولو استوفى ... الخ - اور اگر کسی ایک شریک نے اپنا حصہ دین وصول کر لیا تو دوسرا اس وصول کردہ دین میں شریک ہو جائے گا۔ اور باقی دین کا مطالبہ وہ دونوں مل کر مدیون سے کریں گے اس لئے کہ جب مقبوضہ مقدار میں وہ دونوں شریک ہو گئے تو باقی ماندہ دین بالضرور دونوں کی شرکت پر رہے گا۔
Book of Sulh. ... The principle is that if a debt is common between two partners and one partner collects a portion, the other partner has the option to join in the collected portion or to claim his share from the debtor. The option to join is because the collector obtained an advantage: cash is superior to credit because the value of a debt is realized only upon collection. So the collector has already realized the value, while the other partner has not. This advantage returns to the original right, like the child of a joint slave-girl or the fruit of a joint tree. Before participation, the collected item remains the property of the collector because he took it in exchange for his right, so he becomes its owner. He is liable to his partner for the partner's share. The common debt is that which becomes due through a single cause, like the price of a sold item when sold in a single transaction, or inherited debt, or the price of destroyed common property. Once this is known, the ruling of the book is that the non-settling partner has the option to pursue the original debtor, because the settling partner only collected his own share, so the other's share remains with the debtor. He also has the option to take half the cloth, unless the settling partner guarantees a quarter of the debt. If one partner has already collected his half of the debt, the other partner can join in the collected portion, and then both will claim the remaining debt from the debtor, because when they both share in the collected amount, the remainder necessarily remains jointly owned.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah explains the ruling when two partners have a joint debt, and one partner settles his share by taking a cloth from the debtor. The key principle is that the partner who collects early gains an advantage (cash now vs. future payment). This advantage is analogous to the increase from joint property (e.g., a child from a joint slave-girl or fruit from a joint tree), which is shared. Therefore, the other partner has two options: (1) take half of the cloth (participate in the collection), or (2) pursue the original debtor for his share. However, if the settling partner guarantees to pay a quarter of the debt (i.e., half of the other partner's share), then the other partner loses the right to take the cloth and must accept the guarantee. The passage also clarifies that the collected item remains the property of the collector before participation, but he becomes a guarantor for the partner's share. The definition of 'common debt' is then given: a debt arising from a single cause, such as a sale in one transaction, inheritance, or compensation for destroyed common property. The commentary also addresses a potential objection that sulh against the type of right is a pure exchange, so the partner should have no right in the cloth. The answer distinguishes that sulh in general rulings is like purchase, but in some aspects it is considered an extraction of right.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A settlement or compromise whereby a creditor accepts something in lieu of the debt, often at a discount.
شریک (sharik): A partner in a joint debt or property.
دین مشترک (dayn mushtarak): A debt that is common to two or more persons, due from a single cause.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee; here, the settling partner becomes a guarantor for a quarter of the debt to the other partner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling on joint debt, if one partner settles his share by taking cloth, what options does the other partner have?
A) Only to claim his share from the original debtor
B) To take half the cloth or claim his share from the original debtor
C) To take the entire cloth
D) To cancel the settlement

Key Takeaway
When one partner settles a joint debt, the other partner can share the collected asset or claim the debtor unless a guarantee is given.

Purchase of Goods with Share of Joint Debt
Ruling on purchase by set-off

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one partner purchases goods with his share of a joint debt by set-off and distinguish it from the ruling in sulh.

Core Idea
In a sale, the purchasing partner owns the goods; the other partner can only claim compensation, not the goods.

We have seen that in a settlement (sulh), a partner who does not participate in the compromise can take the goods from the settling partner. But what if the partner uses his share of the debt to purchase goods directly from the debtor through set-off? This is a sale, not a settlement. The fundamental difference between sale (based on full bargaining) and sulh (based on compromise) changes the rights of the other partner. This lesson examines that ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is: one partner uses his share of a joint debt to purchase goods from the debtor by set-off (muqassa). The ruling is: the purchase is valid, and the other partner can demand a guarantee of a quarter of the total debt from the purchasing partner. He cannot take the goods.
The quarter is half of the purchasing partner's share if they are equal partners.
2
Understand the legal basis
The basis is the distinction between sale (bay') and settlement (sulh). Sale is built on bargaining (mumakasa) – the purchaser gets full value for his price. Sulh is built on overlooking and reduction (ighmad wa hatita) – the settling party gives up part of his right. This distinction determines the consequence for the non-participating partner.
In sulh, obliging the settling partner to pay a quarter would cause loss, so the non-settling partner can take the goods. In sale, no loss occurs, so he can only claim compensation.
3
Apply the ruling to an example
Suppose total debt is 100 rupees, each partner's share is 50. Partner A purchases goods worth 50 from the debtor by set-off. Partner B can demand 25 rupees (quarter of total debt) from A as compensation, but cannot take the goods because A owns them by his contract.
4
Contrast with the sulh scenario
If instead Partner A had settled with the debtor for 40 rupees (a compromise), Partner B could take the cloth (goods) from A because A only partially received his right. Here, the purchase is at full value, so no reduction occurred.
This contrast is the key to understanding the ruling.

نے ذکر کیا ہے اور غیر قابض شریک کو خریدنے والے شریک سے کپڑے میں کوئی راہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کا مالک اپنے عقد سے ہوا ہے۔ تشریح قوله ولو اشتری ... الخ - اگر ایک شریک نے اپنے دین کے عوض مدیون سے کوئی چیز خرید لی تو دوسرا شریک چاہے اس سے ربع دین کا تاوان لے۔ جب کہ وہ دونوں مساوی مشارک ہوں اور چاہے اصل مدیون سے مطالبہ کرے جیسا کہ آگے آرہا ہے۔ ربع دین کا تاوان تو اس لئے لے سکتا ہے کہ خریدار شریک تو اپنے حق پر بوجہ مقاصہ پورے طور پر قابض ہو گیا۔ یعنی جب اس نے نصف دین کے برابر قیمت کی چیز خرید لی تو اس کے داموں کا نصف قرضہ سے بدلا ہو گیا اس لئے کہ بیچ کامدار بھر پور دام لگانے پر ہے اور صلح کا مدار چشم پوشی اور کچھ حق ساقط کرنے پر ہے۔ اب اگر مصالح شریک کے ذمہ ربع دین کی ادائیگی لازم کی جائے تو اس سے اس کو خسارہ ہو گا۔ مثلاً سوروپے قرضہ میں سے اس کا حصہ پچاس روپے تھا اور غالباً چالیس روپے پر اس نے صلح کی ہوگی تو اگر اس کے ذمہ ربع دین لازم کریں تو پچاس کا نصف یعنی چھپیں لازم ہوئے۔ حالانکہ اس نے
If one of them purchases goods with his share of the debt, his partner can make him guarantee a quarter of the debt, because the purchaser becomes a full recipient of his right through set-off. This is because sale is based on bargaining, unlike sulh which is based on overlooking and reduction. If we were to oblige him to pay a quarter of the debt, he would suffer loss, so the recipient (the purchaser) has an option as we mentioned. And there is no way for the partner to take the cloth in purchase, because he owns it by his contract and the receipt is by set-off between its price and the debt. Commentary: If one partner purchases something from the debtor in exchange for his share of the debt, the other partner may demand a quarter of the debt as compensation, if they are equal partners. Alternatively, he may claim from the original debtor. The quarter compensation is because the purchaser has fully received his right by set-off. When he purchases goods worth half the debt, the price is offset against half of the debt. Sale is based on full bargaining, while sulh involves overlooking and reduction. If the settling partner were obliged to pay a quarter of the debt, it would be a loss to him. For example, if his share of the debt is 50 rupees and he likely settled for 40, obliging him to pay a quarter (25) would be a loss.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage addresses a separate but related scenario: one partner uses his share of a joint debt to purchase goods directly from the debtor (by set-off). Here, the other partner does NOT have the option to take half the goods (cloth) because this is a sale, not a settlement (sulh). Sale is based on full bargaining, so the purchaser fully owns the goods. However, the other partner can demand a guarantee of a quarter of the debt from the purchasing partner. The reasoning: the purchaser has fully received his right through set-off (مقاصة), so he should compensate his partner for the partner's share of the collected value. The amount is a quarter of the total debt (half of the partner's share). The difference from sulh is emphasized: sulh involves compromise and reduction, so obliging the settling partner to pay a quarter would be a loss; hence the non-settling partner's option to take the cloth is allowed. In purchase, no such loss occurs because the purchase is at full value. The example given: if total debt is 100, partner A's share is 50, he purchases goods worth 50 by set-off; partner B can take 25 (quarter) from A as compensation.

Key Terms
مقاصة (muqassa): Set-off; the cancellation of mutual debts between two parties.
بیع (bay'): Sale; a contract of exchange involving bargaining.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) To cancel the purchase
D) To demand a guarantee of half the debt

Key Takeaway
In a sale by set-off, the purchasing partner owns the goods; the other partner's remedy is compensation, not repossession of the goods.

Options of a Non-Settling Partner After Sulh
Explains the legal options of a non-settling partner after sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to a non-settling partner after a sulh and identify the condition that removes the second option.

Core Idea
A non-settling partner may either pursue the debtor or take the settlement property, unless his partner guarantees his share.

In joint debts, when one partner makes a settlement (sulh) with the debtor, the other partner retains certain rights. This passage from a commentary on the Hidayah clarifies that the non-settling partner has a choice, but that choice is narrowed if the settling partner becomes a guarantor. Understanding this ruling is crucial for properly managing joint claims in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
Recognize that the ruling applies when a debt is jointly owned or when a joint consumable asset has been converted into a debt (e.g., price of a consumed joint property).
The passage begins with examples of joint debts.
2
State the two options
The non-settling partner can either pursue the original debtor for his share or take half of the property (e.g., cloth) that was the subject of the sulh.
The option to take the cloth exists because the non-settling partner has a right of participation (musharakat) in the cloth as well.
3
Identify the condition that restricts the second option
If the settling partner guarantees (becomes damin for) a quarter of the debt, the non-settling partner can no longer take the cloth and must pursue the debtor.
The guarantee shifts the non-settling partner's right back to the original debt.
4
Understand the legal reasoning behind the option
The objection suggests that a sulh against the genus of the right is a pure exchange (mu'awada), giving the non-settling partner no claim on the cloth. The response, citing Bustan al-Khawahir Zadah, explains that such a sulh functions as a purchase in some respects and as a receipt of the right in others, preserving the partnership share.
This clarifies the dual nature of sulh in Hanafi law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Like that debt which is inherited by two persons or the price of a joint consumable item. For example, their joint property was taken by someone [؟]. The text says: 'When you have understood this...' - Now that the aforementioned principles and definition of debt are before you, the ruling of this chapter is that the partner who did not make a settlement (sulh) has the option to pursue the original debtor. Because the settling partner only received his own share; his share remains in the debtor's liability. But the non-settling partner also has a right of participation, and he also has the option to take half of the cloth on which the settlement was made, because he also has a right of participation in the cloth. But if his partner becomes a guarantor for a quarter of the debt, then he cannot take from the cloth, because his right is in the original debt. Question: The right of participation in the cloth should not exist because when the settlement is against the genus of the right, it is a mu'awada (exchange), and in a pure mu'awada, the partner has no way to the cloth. Answer: In the Bustan al-Khawahir Zadah, it is stated that a settlement against the genus of the right is, in general rulings, a purchase (shira'), and in some aspects it is an istifa' (receipt) of the right, and a pure mu'awada is in no way a receipt of part of the right.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a statement from the matn. It first sets the context: when a debt is jointly owned or a joint asset is consumed, and then explains the ruling: a partner who did not participate in a settlement (sulh) with the debtor has two options. First, he can demand his share directly from the debtor, because his right remains in the debtor's liability. Second, he can take half of the cloth that was the subject of the settlement, because he has a right of participation in it. However, if his co-partner (the one who made the sulh) guarantees a quarter of the debt, then the non-settling partner cannot take the cloth and must pursue the debtor. The text then addresses a potential objection: since the sulh was against the genus of the right (i.e., taking cloth instead of money), it should be a pure exchange (mu'awada) where the partner has no share. The answer, citing Bustan al-Khawahir Zadah, clarifies that such a sulh is considered a purchase in many rulings, and in some aspects it is a receipt of the right, so the partner does have a share.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A settlement or compromise where a creditor agrees to take something other than the original debt to discharge it.
مشارکت (musharakat): Shared right of ownership or claim between partners in a joint property or debt.
ضامن (damin): A guarantor who becomes liable for a portion of the debt, here the settling partner guarantees a quarter of the debt to the non-settling partner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if the debtor fails to pay.

Key Takeaway
The non-settling partner's right to the settlement property is conditional on the settling partner not guaranteeing the debt.

Options When a Partner Purchases Goods Using His Share of Joint Debt
Ruling with proof on partner's options after set-off purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options available to a partner when his co-partner uses their joint debt to purchase goods via set-off, and explain the reasoning based on the distinction between sale and compromise.

Core Idea
When one partner buys goods with his share of joint debt, the other may take a quarter from him or pursue the debtor.

In a partnership where one partner receives his share of a joint debt or uses it to buy goods, the other partner's rights are affected. This lesson explains the specific options when a purchase is made via set-off (muqassa), based on the commentary from 'Ashraf ul Hadaya'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A joint debt is owed to two partners. One partner buys goods from the debtor using his share of the debt as a price via set-off.
The partners are assumed to be equal owners of the joint debt unless stated otherwise.
2
State the ruling
The non-buying partner has two choices: (a) take a quarter of the total joint debt from the buying partner as compensation, or (b) demand the remaining debt from the debtor.
The quarter of the debt is the fraction that corresponds to the buying partner's share in the set-off. For equal partners, it's quarter of the total debt.
3
Understand the reasoning for the quarter
The buyer is considered to have fully received his right via set-off, but since a sale is based on full pricing (unlike a compromise), the buyer is not required to share the goods. The quarter compensates the other partner for his share of the debt that was used.
In a compromise (sulh), the partner might have accepted a reduction; forcing payment of a quarter would cause loss, so the receiver is given a choice.
4
Note the condition and variation
This ruling applies when partners are equal in their shares. If shares are unequal, the fraction adjusts: the non-buying partner can take his proportion of the debt from the buyer or demand his full share from the debtor.
The text explicitly mentions quarter for equal shares.
5
Distinguish from compromise (sulh)
In a compromise, the partner who settles for less than his full share does not have to pay a quarter because the compromise involves reduction; forcing payment would cause him loss. Hence, in sulh, the non-settling partner has different options (to be covered in other texts).
This distinction is key to understanding why the quarter option exists only in a sale (bay').

قوله ولو استوفى ... الخ - اور اگر کسی ایک شریک نے اپنا حصہ دین وصول کر لیا تو دوسرا اس وصول کردہ دین میں شریک ہو جائے گا۔ اور باقی دین کا مطالبہ وہ دونوں مل کر مدیون سے کریں گے اس لئے کہ جب مقبوضہ مقدار میں وہ دونوں شریک ہو گئے تو باقی ماندہ دین بالضرور دونوں کی شرکت پر رہے گا۔ ایک شریک نے اپنے دین کے بدلے سامان خریدا تو دوسرا شریک ربع دین کا ضامن بنا سکتا ہے قَالَ وَلَوِ اشْتَرى أَحَدُهُمَا بِنَصِيبِهِ مِنَ الدَّيْنِ سِلْعَةَ كَانَ لِشَرِيكِهِ أَنْ يُضَمَنَهُ رُبُعُ الدَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُ صَارَ قَابِضًا حَقَّهُ بِالْمُقَاصَةِ كَمَلًا لِاَنَّ مَبْنَى الْبَيْعَ عَلَى الْمُمَاكَسَةِ بِخِلَافِ الصُّلْحُ لِاَنَّ مَبْنَاهُ عَلَى الْإِغْمَاضِ وَالْحَطِيطَةَ فَلَوْ الْزَمْنَاهُ دَفَعَ رُبعَ الدِّينِ يَتَضَرَّرُ بِهِ فَيَتَخَيَّرَ الْقَابِضُ كَمَا ذَكَرْنَاهَ وَلَا سَبِيْلَ لِلشَّرِيكِ عَلَى التَّوْبِ فِي الْبَيْعِ لِأَنَّهُ ملكَهُ بِعَقْدِهِ وَالْإِسْتِيْفَاءُ بِالْمَقَاصَةِ بَيْنَ ثَمَنِهِ وَبَيْنَ الدَّين ہا ہے۔ ترجمہ اگر خرید لیا ان میں سے ایک نے اپنے حصہ کے دین سے کچھ اسباب تو اس کا شریک اس سے چوتھائی قرضہ کا تاوان لے سکتا ہے کیونکہ خریدنے والا تو اپنے حق پر بوجہ مقاصہ بھر پور قابض ہو گیا۔ اس لئے کہ بیچ تو کس کر دام لگانے پر مبنی ہے بخلاف صلح کے کہ اس کا مدار چشم پوشی اور کچھ حق ساقط کرنے پر ہے۔ پس اگر صلح کنندہ کے ذمہ چوتھائی قرضہ دینا لازم کریں تو اس سے ضرر اٹھائے گا۔ لہذا قابض کو اختیار دیا گیا جیسا کہ ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے اور غیر قابض شریک کو خریدنے والے شریک سے کپڑے میں کوئی راہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کا مالک اپنے عقد سے ہوا ہے۔ تشریح قوله ولو اشتری ... الخ - اگر ایک شریک نے اپنے دین کے عوض مدیون سے کوئی چیز خرید لی تو دوسرا شریک چاہے اس سے ربع دین کا تاوان لے۔ جب کہ وہ دونوں مساوی مشارک ہوں اور چاہے اصل مدیون سے مطالبہ کرے جیسا کہ آگے آرہا ہے۔ ربع دین کا تاوان تو اس لئے لے سکتا ہے کہ خریدار شریک تو اپنے حق پر بوجہ مقاصہ پورے طور پر قابض ہو گیا۔ یعنی جب اس نے نصف دین کے برابر قیمت کی چیز خرید لی تو اس کے داموں کا نصف قرضہ سے بدلا ہو گیا اس لئے کہ بیچ کامدار بھر پور دام لگانے پر ہے اور صلح کا مدار چشم پوشی اور کچھ حق ساقط کرنے پر ہے۔ اب اگر مصالح شریک کے ذمہ ربع دین کی ادائیگی لازم کی جائے تو اس سے اس کو خسارہ ہو گا۔ مثلاً سوروپے قرضہ میں سے اس کا حصہ پچاس روپے تھا اور غالباً چالیس روپے پر اس نے صلح کی ہوگی تو اگر اس کے ذمہ ربع دین لازم کریں تو پچاس کا نصف یعنی چھپیں لازم ہوئے۔ حالانکہ اس نے صرف چالیس ہی پائے ہیں جس کا نصف میں ہے تو چوتھائی قرضہ لازم کرنے میں اس کو پانچ روپے کا خسارہ ہوگا۔ لہذا اس کو از چاہے آدھا مصالح علیہ دے دے اور چاہے چوتھائی قرضہ دے دے پھر غیر قابض شریک کو بیع کی صورت میں مشتری ثوب شریک کے ساتھ کپڑے میں شرکت کرنے کی کوئی راہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کا مالک اپنے عقد بیع سے ہوا ہے نہ کہ دین کے سبب سے۔ قوله والاستيفاء.... الخ - سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ یہ تو تسلیم ہے کہ کپڑا خریدنے والا شریک اپنے عقد بیع سے اس کا مالک ہوا ہے۔ لیکن اس کا عقد تو دین مشترک کے بعض حصہ کے عوض میں ہوا ہے اور یہ مقبوض میں اشتراک کا مقتضی ہے۔ پھر کیسے کہتے ہو کہ غیر قابض شریک کو کپڑے میں شرکت کی کوئی راہ نہیں ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ استیفاء حصہ مشترک کے مقابلہ میں نہیں ہوا بلکہ اس ثمن کے مقابلہ میں ہوا ہے جو بطریق مقاصہ اس کے لئے مخصوص ہوا ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد بیع۔ ذمہ مشتری میں ثبوت ثمن کا مقتضی ہے اور عقد کے وقت اس کے حصہ کا فریم کی طرف منسوب ہونا اس کے منافی نہیں ہے کیونکہ نفوذ عین ہوں یا دین عقود میں متعین نہیں ہوتے۔
The text says: 'And if he received...' - If one of the two partners received his share of the debt, then the other partner will share in that received debt. And they will both jointly demand the remaining debt from the debtor, because when they both share in the received amount, the remaining debt necessarily remains as a joint claim between them. One partner bought goods in exchange for his share of the debt; then the other partner can make him a guarantor for a quarter of the debt. He said: 'And if one of them buys a commodity with his share of the debt, his partner can take a quarter of the debt from him as a guarantee, because he has become a fully receiving party of his right through set-off (muqassa). This is because a sale is based on bargaining, unlike a compromise (sulh) which is based on forbearance and reduction. If we were to oblige him to pay a quarter of the debt, he would suffer loss. So the receiver is given a choice, as we have mentioned. And the partner has no recourse to the cloth in a sale because he owned it by his contract.' Translation: If one of them buys some goods with his share of the debt, his partner can take a quarter of the debt from him as compensation, because the buyer has become fully in receipt of his right through set-off (muqassa). This is because a sale is based on striking a full price, unlike a compromise which is based on forbearance and relinquishment of part of the right. So if we oblige the compromising partner to pay a quarter of the debt, it would cause him loss. Hence the receiver is given a choice, as we have mentioned. And the non-receiving partner has no way to the cloth from the buying partner, because he owned it by his own contract. Explanation of the text: If one partner buys something from the debtor in exchange for his share of the debt, the other partner may either take a quarter of the debt from him as compensation (when they are equal partners) or demand it from the original debtor, as will come later. He can take a quarter because the buyer partner has fully received his right via set-off. That is, when he buys goods worth half the debt, his price is exchanged for half the debt, because a sale is based on full pricing, while a compromise is based on forbearance and reduction. If we oblige the compromising partner to pay a quarter of the debt, he suffers loss. For example, if the joint debt is 100 rupees and his share is 50, and he likely made a compromise for 40 rupees, if we oblige him to pay a quarter of the debt (i.e., 25 rupees), he would have lost 5 rupees. Therefore, he has the choice: either give half of the compromise item or give a quarter of the debt. Then, in the case of a sale, the non-receiving partner has no way to participate in the cloth owned by the buying partner, because he owns it by his sale contract, not due to the debt. The text says: 'And the receipt...' - This is an answer to an implied question. The question is: It is conceded that the partner who bought the cloth owns it by his sale contract, but his contract was in exchange for part of the joint debt, which requires sharing in what is received. So why do you say the non-receiving partner has no way to participate in the cloth? The gist of the answer is that the receipt (istifa') was not against the joint share but against the price that became specific to him through set-off. Because a sale contract necessitates the establishment of a price in the buyer's liability, and at the time of the contract, attributing his share to the price is not contradictory to this, because debts, whether specific (‘ayn) or liabilities (dayn), are not specified in contracts.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that presents two distinct rulings. First, if one partner physically receives his share of the joint debt, the other partner automatically shares in that received amount, and the remaining debt is still jointly claimed. Second, if one partner uses his share of the debt to purchase goods from the debtor (via set-off), the other partner has the option to either take a quarter of the debt as compensation from the buying partner or pursue the debtor directly. The key distinction is that a sale (bay') is based on full pricing, while a compromise (sulh) is based on forbearance; therefore, forcing the buying partner to pay a quarter would cause him loss if he had made a compromise. The text also clarifies that in a sale, the non-buying partner cannot claim a share in the goods because the buyer owns them by his own contract. A question and answer section explains that although the purchase was made against the joint debt, the receipt was against the price that became specific to the buyer through set-off, not against the joint share directly.

Key Terms
مقاصہ (muqassa): Set-off; offsetting a debt against a price, effectively paying through mutual cancellation.
بیع (bay'): A sale contract based on full pricing and bargaining.
ربع دین (rub' al-dayn): Quarter of the debt; the compensation the non-buying partner can take from the buying partner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason that the non-buying partner can take a quarter of the debt from the buying partner in a sale?
A) Because the buyer fully receives his right via set-off and owes compensation for using the joint debt.
B) Because the buyer did not actually pay the debtor.
C) Because the buyer made a profit on the goods.
D) Because the partner is a co-owner of the goods.

Key Takeaway
When one partner buys goods with his share of a joint debt via set-off in a sale, the other partner may take a quarter of the debt from him or pursue the debtor; he cannot claim the goods.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
7 min
Why the Non-Buying Partner Cannot Claim a Share in the Goods Purchased
Expansion on why the non-buying partner has no share in goods purchased via set-off

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain, using the commentary's reasoning, why the non-buying partner does not have a share in goods purchased by his co-partner using the joint debt.

Core Idea
The buyer owns the goods by his sale contract, not due to the debt; receipt via set-off is against the price, not the joint share.

A common misconception is that if one partner uses a joint debt to buy goods, the goods become jointly owned. This lesson clarifies the legal reasoning behind the Hanafi ruling that the non-buying partner has no claim to the goods, focusing on the nature of set-off and the contract of sale.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the implied question
The text anticipates a question: if the purchase was made against the joint debt, why doesn't the other partner share in the goods?
This is a standard dialectical method in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Understand the answer: receipt is against the price
The receipt (istifa') via set-off is not against the joint share of the debt, but against the price that became specific to the buyer through the sale contract.
The price is a liability on the buyer; set-off extinguishes that liability using his share of the joint debt.
3
Note the specificity of set-off in a sale
In a sale, the buyer owes a price. When set-off occurs, it is the price that is cancelled, not a portion of the joint debt directly. The joint debt remains partially intact for the other partner.
Thus, the goods are owned by the buyer in exchange for the price, not as a direct acquisition from the joint debt.
4
Apply the principle: ownership arises from the contract
The buyer owns the goods by virtue of his own contract of sale (bay‘), not by reason of the debt relationship. The debt relationship only gave him the right to use his share as payment.
This is a contractual ownership, not co-ownership via debt.
5
Conclude the legal consequence
Therefore, the non-buying partner has no claim on the goods. His only recourse is to seek compensation from the buyer (quarter) or pursue the debtor for his share of the remaining debt.
This protects the finality of sale contracts and ownership.

قوله ولو استوفى ... الخ - اور اگر کسی ایک شریک نے اپنا حصہ دین وصول کر لیا تو دوسرا اس وصول کردہ دین میں شریک ہو جائے گا۔ اور باقی دین کا مطالبہ وہ دونوں مل کر مدیون سے کریں گے اس لئے کہ جب مقبوضہ مقدار میں وہ دونوں شریک ہو گئے تو باقی ماندہ دین بالضرور دونوں کی شرکت پر رہے گا۔ ایک شریک نے اپنے دین کے بدلے سامان خریدا تو دوسرا شریک ربع دین کا ضامن بنا سکتا ہے قَالَ وَلَوِ اشْتَرى أَحَدُهُمَا بِنَصِيبِهِ مِنَ الدَّيْنِ سِلْعَةَ كَانَ لِشَرِيكِهِ أَنْ يُضَمَنَهُ رُبُعُ الدَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُ صَارَ قَابِضًا حَقَّهُ بِالْمُقَاصَةِ كَمَلًا لِاَنَّ مَبْنَى الْبَيْعَ عَلَى الْمُمَاكَسَةِ بِخِلَافِ الصُّلْحُ لِاَنَّ مَبْنَاهُ عَلَى الْإِغْمَاضِ وَالْحَطِيطَةَ فَلَوْ الْزَمْنَاهُ دَفَعَ رُبعَ الدِّينِ يَتَضَرَّرُ بِهِ فَيَتَخَيَّرَ الْقَابِضُ كَمَا ذَكَرْنَاهَ وَلَا سَبِيْلَ لِلشَّرِيكِ عَلَى التَّوْبِ فِي الْبَيْعِ لِأَنَّهُ ملكَهُ بِعَقْدِهِ وَالْإِسْتِيْفَاءُ بِالْمَقَاصَةِ بَيْنَ ثَمَنِهِ وَبَيْنَ الدَّين ہا ہے۔ ترجمہ اگر خرید لیا ان میں سے ایک نے اپنے حصہ کے دین سے کچھ اسباب تو اس کا شریک اس سے چوتھائی قرضہ کا تاوان لے سکتا ہے کیونکہ خریدنے والا تو اپنے حق پر بوجہ مقاصہ بھر پور قابض ہو گیا۔ اس لئے کہ بیچ تو کس کر دام لگانے پر مبنی ہے بخلاف صلح کے کہ اس کا مدار چشم پوشی اور کچھ حق ساقط کرنے پر ہے۔ پس اگر صلح کنندہ کے ذمہ چوتھائی قرضہ دینا لازم کریں تو اس سے ضرر اٹھائے گا۔ لہذا قابض کو اختیار دیا گیا جیسا کہ ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے اور غیر قابض شریک کو خریدنے والے شریک سے کپڑے میں کوئی راہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کا مالک اپنے عقد سے ہوا ہے۔ تشریح قوله ولو اشتری ... الخ - اگر ایک شریک نے اپنے دین کے عوض مدیون سے کوئی چیز خرید لی تو دوسرا شریک چاہے اس سے ربع دین کا تاوان لے۔ جب کہ وہ دونوں مساوی مشارک ہوں اور چاہے اصل مدیون سے مطالبہ کرے جیسا کہ آگے آرہا ہے۔ ربع دین کا تاوان تو اس لئے لے سکتا ہے کہ خریدار شریک تو اپنے حق پر بوجہ مقاصہ پورے طور پر قابض ہو گیا۔ یعنی جب اس نے نصف دین کے برابر قیمت کی چیز خرید لی تو اس کے داموں کا نصف قرضہ سے بدلا ہو گیا اس لئے کہ بیچ کامدار بھر پور دام لگانے پر ہے اور صلح کا مدار چشم پوشی اور کچھ حق ساقط کرنے پر ہے۔ اب اگر مصالح شریک کے ذمہ ربع دین کی ادائیگی لازم کی جائے تو اس سے اس کو خسارہ ہو گا۔ مثلاً سوروپے قرضہ میں سے اس کا حصہ پچاس روپے تھا اور غالباً چالیس روپے پر اس نے صلح کی ہوگی تو اگر اس کے ذمہ ربع دین لازم کریں تو پچاس کا نصف یعنی چھپیں لازم ہوئے۔ حالانکہ اس نے صرف چالیس ہی پائے ہیں جس کا نصف میں ہے تو چوتھائی قرضہ لازم کرنے میں اس کو پانچ روپے کا خسارہ ہوگا۔ لہذا اس کو از چاہے آدھا مصالح علیہ دے دے اور چاہے چوتھائی قرضہ دے دے پھر غیر قابض شریک کو بیع کی صورت میں مشتری ثوب شریک کے ساتھ کپڑے میں شرکت کرنے کی کوئی راہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کا مالک اپنے عقد بیع سے ہوا ہے نہ کہ دین کے سبب سے۔ قوله والاستيفاء.... الخ - سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ یہ تو تسلیم ہے کہ کپڑا خریدنے والا شریک اپنے عقد بیع سے اس کا مالک ہوا ہے۔ لیکن اس کا عقد تو دین مشترک کے بعض حصہ کے عوض میں ہوا ہے اور یہ مقبوض میں اشتراک کا مقتضی ہے۔ پھر کیسے کہتے ہو کہ غیر قابض شریک کو کپڑے میں شرکت کی کوئی راہ نہیں ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ استیفاء حصہ مشترک کے مقابلہ میں نہیں ہوا بلکہ اس ثمن کے مقابلہ میں ہوا ہے جو بطریق مقاصہ اس کے لئے مخصوص ہوا ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد بیع۔ ذمہ مشتری میں ثبوت ثمن کا مقتضی ہے اور عقد کے وقت اس کے حصہ کا فریم کی طرف منسوب ہونا اس کے منافی نہیں ہے کیونکہ نفوذ عین ہوں یا دین عقود میں متعین نہیں ہوتے۔
The text says: 'And if he received...' - If one of the two partners received his share of the debt, then the other partner will share in that received debt. And they will both jointly demand the remaining debt from the debtor, because when they both share in the received amount, the remaining debt necessarily remains as a joint claim between them. One partner bought goods in exchange for his share of the debt; then the other partner can make him a guarantor for a quarter of the debt. He said: 'And if one of them buys a commodity with his share of the debt, his partner can take a quarter of the debt from him as a guarantee, because he has become a fully receiving party of his right through set-off (muqassa). This is because a sale is based on bargaining, unlike a compromise (sulh) which is based on forbearance and reduction. If we were to oblige him to pay a quarter of the debt, he would suffer loss. So the receiver is given a choice, as we have mentioned. And the partner has no recourse to the cloth in a sale because he owned it by his contract.' Translation: If one of them buys some goods with his share of the debt, his partner can take a quarter of the debt from him as compensation, because the buyer has become fully in receipt of his right through set-off (muqassa). This is because a sale is based on striking a full price, unlike a compromise which is based on forbearance and relinquishment of part of the right. So if we oblige the compromising partner to pay a quarter of the debt, it would cause him loss. Hence the receiver is given a choice, as we have mentioned. And the non-receiving partner has no way to the cloth from the buying partner, because he owned it by his own contract. Explanation of the text: If one partner buys something from the debtor in exchange for his share of the debt, the other partner may either take a quarter of the debt from him as compensation (when they are equal partners) or demand it from the original debtor, as will come later. He can take a quarter because the buyer partner has fully received his right via set-off. That is, when he buys goods worth half the debt, his price is exchanged for half the debt, because a sale is based on full pricing, while a compromise is based on forbearance and reduction. If we oblige the compromising partner to pay a quarter of the debt, he suffers loss. For example, if the joint debt is 100 rupees and his share is 50, and he likely made a compromise for 40 rupees, if we oblige him to pay a quarter of the debt (i.e., 25 rupees), he would have lost 5 rupees. Therefore, he has the choice: either give half of the compromise item or give a quarter of the debt. Then, in the case of a sale, the non-receiving partner has no way to participate in the cloth owned by the buying partner, because he owns it by his sale contract, not due to the debt. The text says: 'And the receipt...' - This is an answer to an implied question. The question is: It is conceded that the partner who bought the cloth owns it by his sale contract, but his contract was in exchange for part of the joint debt, which requires sharing in what is received. So why do you say the non-receiving partner has no way to participate in the cloth? The gist of the answer is that the receipt (istifa') was not against the joint share but against the price that became specific to him through set-off. Because a sale contract necessitates the establishment of a price in the buyer's liability, and at the time of the contract, attributing his share to the price is not contradictory to this, because debts, whether specific (‘ayn) or liabilities (dayn), are not specified in contracts.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that presents two distinct rulings. First, if one partner physically receives his share of the joint debt, the other partner automatically shares in that received amount, and the remaining debt is still jointly claimed. Second, if one partner uses his share of the debt to purchase goods from the debtor (via set-off), the other partner has the option to either take a quarter of the debt as compensation from the buying partner or pursue the debtor directly. The key distinction is that a sale (bay') is based on full pricing, while a compromise (sulh) is based on forbearance; therefore, forcing the buying partner to pay a quarter would cause him loss if he had made a compromise. The text also clarifies that in a sale, the non-buying partner cannot claim a share in the goods because the buyer owns them by his own contract. A question and answer section explains that although the purchase was made against the joint debt, the receipt was against the price that became specific to the buyer through set-off, not against the joint share directly.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): Price; the consideration in a sale contract.
استیفاء (istifa'): Receipt or full acquisition of one's right; here used for the buyer's receipt via set-off.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, the receipt (istifa') of the buyer via set-off is against what?
A) The joint share of the debt.
B) The price that becomes specific to him through set-off.
C) The entire joint debt.
D) The goods themselves.

Key Takeaway
The buyer's set-off extinguishes the price, not the joint share; thus the goods are owned by the buyer alone, and the partner has no claim to them.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
General Right of a Partner to Pursue the Debtor and Specific Scenarios
Establishes the partner's general right to follow the debtor and enumerates scenarios affecting that right.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that a non-receiving partner may always pursue the debtor for his share of a joint debt, and classify specific actions as either constructive receipt (qabd) or destruction (itlaf), including the intra-Hanafi disagreement on granting a delay and burning.

Core Idea
A partner in a joint debt always retains the right to pursue the debtor until his share is received; actions like release or set-off are destruction, not receipt.

In a joint debt where one partner has already received his share from the debtor (either physically or constructively), does the other partner lose his right to pursue the debtor? The default rule is that his right remains – he can still follow the debtor because the receiving partner’s receipt does not extinguish the non-receiver’s claim. This passage from the Hidayah elaborates this principle and then walks through a series of scenarios: handing over what was received, set-off, release, granting a delay, usurpation, invalid purchase, hiring, burning, marriage, and compromise. Each scenario illustrates whether the non-receiver’s action counts as ‘qabd’ (receipt) or ‘itlaf’ (destruction), which determines whether he can later reclaim participation from the receiving partner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its basis
Read the opening sentence: 'And the partner has the right to follow the debtor in all that we have mentioned, because his right in his liability remains.' Note that the reason given is that the receiver actually received his share, but the non-receiver still has a right of participation – he may choose not to participate.
The right remains even after the receiver obtains his share.
2
Recognize the actions that affect the non-receiver's right
The passage lists multiple actions: handing over to receiver (taslim), set-off (muqassa), release (ibra'), granting a delay (ta'khir), usurpation (ghasb), invalid purchase (shira' fasid) with destruction, hiring (istijar), burning (ihraq), marriage (tazwij), and compromise (sulh). For each, note whether it is considered qabd or itlaf.
Qabd preserves the right to participate; itlaf extinguishes it.
3
Determine the classification for each action
Go through each: Handing over after loss → still can participate (because condition not met). Set-off → itlaf (discharge, not receipt). Release → itlaf. Granting delay → disputed (Abu Yusuf: valid by qiyas to ibra'; majority: invalid). Usurp/invalid purchase with destruction → qabd (constructive receipt). Hiring → qabd. Burning → disputed (Muhammad: qabd; Abu Yusuf: not). Marriage → itlaf (Zahir al-Riwayah). Compromise for intentional injury → itlaf.
The ikhtilaf on delay and burning shows the importance of analogy.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on granting a delay
Focus on the ta'khir case. Abu Yusuf analogizes ta'khir to absolute ibra' (both relinquish the right to immediate collection). The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) reject the analogy because ta'khir does not remove the debt but defers it, leading to division of debt before receipt – which is prohibited.
The practical consequence (thamarah): if valid, the deferral is binding and the other partner cannot claim that share; if invalid, the debtor's obligation remains unchanged.
5
Apply the framework to a new scenario
Suppose the non-receiving partner gives the debtor a gift of his share (hiba). Using the reasoning from the passage, would this be qabd or itlaf? Compare to ibra' (release) which is itlaf, so hiba would likely be itlaf. But check if it resembles 'destruction' of the right to claim.
Always check the illa: does the action completely extinguish the right or merely change its mode? If it extinguishes, it's itlaf; if it puts the partner in control of the asset, it's qabd.
