تمام مسائل مذکورہ میں شریک مدیون کا دامن گیر ہو وَلِلشَّرِيكِ أَنْ يَتَّبِعَ الْغَرِيْمَ فِي جَمِيعِ مَا ذَكَرْنَا لِأَنَّ حَقَّهُ فِي ذِمَّتِهِ بَاقِ لِأَنَّ الْقَابِضَ اسْتَوْقَى نَصِيبَهُ حَقِيقَةً لَكِنَّ لَهُ حَقُّ الْمُشَارَكَةِ فَلَهُ أَنْ لَا يُشَارِكَهُ فَلَوْ سَلَّمَ لَهُ مَا قَبَضَ ثُمَّ تَوَى مَا عَلَى الْغَرِيْمِ لَهُ أَنْ يُشَارِكَ الْقَابِضَ لِأَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا رَضِيَ بِالتَّسْلِيمِ لِيُسَلَّمَ لَهُ مَا فِي ذِمَّةِ الْغَرِيمِ وَلَمْ يُسَلَّمَ وَلَوْ وَقَعَتِ الْمُقَاصَّةُ بِدَيْنٍ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ قَبْلِ لَمْ يَرْجِعُ عَلَيْهِ الشَرِيكَ لأَنَّهُ قَاضِ بِنَصِيبِهِ لَا مُقْتَضِ وَلَوْ اَبْرَاهُ عَنْ نَصِيبِهِ فَكَذَلِكَ لِأَنَّهُ إِثْلَاتٌ وَلَيْسَ بِقَبْضِ وَلَوْ إِبْرَاهِ عَنِ الْبَعْضِ كَانَتْ قِسْمَةُ الْبَاقِي عَلَى مَا بَقِيَ مِنَ السِّهَامِ وَلَوْ أَخَّرَ اَحَدُهُمَا عَنْ نَصِيبِهِ صَحَ عِنْدَ أَبِي وسُفَ اِعْتِبَارًا بِالْإِبْرَاءِ الْمُطْلَقِ وَلَا يَصِحُ عِنْدَهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ يُؤَدِى إِلَى قِسْمَةِ الدَّيْنِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ وَلَوْ غَصَبَ اَحَدُهُمَا عَيْنًا مِنْهُ أَوِ اشْتَرَاهُ شِرَاءً فَاسِدًا وَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ فَهُوَ قَبْضٌ وَالْإِسْتِيْجَارُ بِنَصِيبِهِ قَبْضٌ وَكَذَا الْإِحْرَاقُ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ خِلَافًا لَابِى يُوسُفَ وَالتَّزَوُّجُ بِهِ اِثْلَاثِ فِى ظَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَةِ وَكَذَا الصُّلْحُ عَلَيْهِ عَنْ جِنَايَةِ الْعَمَدِ ترجمہ اور غیر قابض شریک کو اختیار ہے کہ مدیون کا دامن گیر ہو۔ ان تمام صورتوں میں جو ہم نے ذکر کیں۔ کیونکہ اس کا حق اس کے ذمہ باقی ہے اس لئے کہ قابض نے در حقیقت اپنا حصہ وصول کیا ہے۔ لیکن اس کے لئے حق مشارکت ہے تو اس کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ مشارکت نہ کرے۔ پھر اگر شریک نے وصول کنندہ کو وہ سپر درکھا جو اس نے وصول کیا ہے اور جو مدیوں پر باقی تھا وہ ڈوب گیا تو اس کو اختیار ہے قابض کے ساتھ مشارکت کا۔ کیونکہ وہ سپر دکرنے پر اسی لئے راضی ہوا تھا تا کہ اس کو وہ ملے جو مدیون کے ذمہ ہے اور وہ اس کو نہیں ملا۔ اور اگر مقاصد اس دین سے ہوا جوکسی شریک پر پہلے سے تھا تو دوسرا شریک اس سے کچھ نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے حصہ سے قرض چکانے والا ہے وصول کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور اگر اپنے حصہ سے مدیون کو بری کر دیا تب بھی یوں ہی ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ اختلاف ہے نہ کہ قبضہ۔ اور اگر بعض حصہ سے بری کیا تو باقی قرضہ کی تقسیم باقی ماندہ حق کے موافق حقہ رسد ہوگی ۔ اور اگر کسی شریک نے مدیون کو اپنے حصہ کی مہلت دے دی تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک صحیح ہے ابراء مطلق پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور طرفین کے نزدیک صحیح نہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ قبضہ سے پہلے قرضہ کے ہزارہ کی طرف مفضی ہے اور اگر کسی شریک نے مدیون سے کوئی چیز نصب کر لی یا بطریق فاسد خرید لی اور وہ اس کے پاس تلف ہو گئی تو یہ قبضہ ہے اور اگر اپنے حصہ کے عوض کوئی چیز اجارہ پر لی تو یہ بھی قبضہ ہے۔ اور اسی طرح جلانا امام محمد کے نزدیک برخلاف امام ابو یوسف کے۔ اور اپنے حصہ پر نکاح کرنا اتلاف ہے۔ ظاہر الروایہ میں اسی طرح اپنے حصہ پر جنابت عمد سے صلح کرنا۔
In all these mentioned cases, the partner is the pursuer of the debtor. 'And the partner has the right to follow the debtor in all that we have mentioned, because his right in his liability remains, because the receiver actually received his share, but he has a right of participation, so he may choose not to participate. Then if the partner hands over what he received, and then what was on the debtor is lost, he has the right to participate with the receiver, because he only agreed to hand over in order to secure what was in the debtor's liability, and it was not secured. And if the set-off (muqassa) occurs with a debt that he owed from before, the partner cannot recourse against him, because he is discharging his share, not receiving. And if he releases him (the debtor) from his share, the same applies, because it is a destruction (itlaf), not a receipt (qabd). And if he releases him from part of it, the remainder is divided according to the remaining shares. And if one of them gives a delay for his share, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf, by analogy to the absolute release (ibra' mutlaq), and it is not valid according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), because it leads to division of a debt before receipt. And if one of them usurps an 'ayn (specific item) from him or buys it with a fasid (invalid) purchase and it is destroyed in his hand, then it is qabd (possession). And hiring (istijar) with his share is qabd. Similarly, burning is qabd according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. And marrying with it is itlaf (destruction) in the Zahir al-Riwayah. Similarly, making a compromise (sulh) on it for intentional injury (jinayat al-'amd).' Translation: And the non-receiving partner has the option to pursue the debtor in all these cases we have mentioned, because his right remains in his liability; because the receiver actually received his share, but he has a right of participation, so he has the option not to participate. Then if the partner hands over to the receiver what he received, and then what was on the debtor is lost, he has the option to participate with the receiver, because he only agreed to the handover so that he would receive what was in the debtor's liability, and it was not received. And if the set-off (muqassa) occurs with a debt that was owed by one partner from before, the other partner cannot take anything from him, because he is paying off his share, not receiving. And if he releases the debtor from his share, it is the same, because this is destruction (itlaf), not receipt (qabd). And if he releases from part of the share, the remaining debt is divided according to the remaining shares. And if one partner gives the debtor a delay for his share, it is valid according to Imam Abu Yusuf, by analogy to absolute release (ibra' mutlaq), and not valid according to the two (Imams Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), because it leads to division of a debt before receipt. And if one partner usurps an item from the debtor, or buys it with an invalid purchase (shira' fasid) and it is destroyed in his hand, then this is considered qabd (possession). And hiring something with his share is also qabd. Similarly, burning is qabd according to Imam Muhammad, contrary to Imam Abu Yusuf. And marrying (with the share of the debt) is itlaf (destruction) in the Zahir al-Riwayah. Similarly, making a compromise (sulh) on it for intentional injury (jinayat 'amd) is also itlaf.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that establishes a general rule: in all the cases mentioned, the non-receiving partner may always pursue the debtor because his right remains in the debtor's liability. The receiver received his own share, but the non-receiver still has a right of participation. The text then elaborates various specific scenarios: (1) If the non-receiver hands over what he received to the receiver and later the debtor's debt becomes irrecoverable, he can reclaim participation with the receiver. (2) If there is a set-off with a debt the non-receiver owed to the receiver, he cannot claim anything from the receiver because it is a discharge of his own debt, not a receipt. (3) If he releases the debtor from his share, it is not a receipt but a destruction (itlaf). (4) If he releases part of his share, the remaining debt is divided proportionally. (5) If he grants a delay to the debtor for his share, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf considers it valid by analogy to absolute release, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it invalid because it amounts to division of debt before receipt. (6) If a partner usurps an item, buys it invalidly (fasad), or hires it with his share, and it is destroyed in his possession, that is considered qabd (receipt) of his share. (7) Burning is considered qabd according to Muhammad but not according to Abu Yusuf. (8) Marrying using the share of debt is itlaf. (9) Making a compromise (sulh) on the debt in return for forgiveness of intentional injury (jinayat 'amd) is also itlaf. These rulings clarify when the partner's right to participate or follow the debtor is affected.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Possession or receipt; acts that put the partner in a position of having taken his share, even if not physically received, such as usurpation or invalid purchase leading to destruction.
اتلاف (itlaf): Destruction or disposition that extinguishes the right, such as releasing the debtor or marrying the share.
ابراء (ibra'): Release from a debt; absolving the debtor of liability for one's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a partner gives the debtor a delay for his share of the joint debt?
A) It is valid according to all Hanafi imams.
B) It is invalid according to all Hanafi imams.
C) It is valid according to Abu Yusuf but invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
D) It is valid only if the other partner agrees.

Key Takeaway
A partner in a joint debt may always pursue the debtor for his share unless he has performed a constructive receipt (qabd) or a destruction (itlaf) of his right; actions like release, set-off, marriage, and compromise are itlaf, while usurpation, invalid purchase, hiring, and burning (according to Muhammad) are qabd.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Non-possessing partner's rights and the dispute on ta'khir
States the non-possessing partner's rights and the dispute on ta'khir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rights of a non-possessing partner in a partnership debt and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'khir (deferment) with its legal basis.

Core Idea
A partner cannot defer his share of a shared debt pre-possession, as it effectively divides the debt, unlike ibra which destroys the right.

This passage from Kitab al-Sulh addresses situations where one partner has collected from a common debtor. The non-possessing partner retains a right to pursue the debtor and may even join in what was collected if the debtor's remaining debt is lost. The key dispute is whether giving the debtor more time (ta'khir) is valid; the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say no, because it leads to division of debt before possession, while Abu Yusuf allows it by analogy with absolute release (ibra mutlaq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the partner scenarios
The passage discusses a partnership where one partner (the qabid) has collected from the common debtor, and the other (the non-possessing partner) has not. Understand the basic right: the non-possessing partner may pursue the debtor directly or choose to participate in what was collected.
This right exists because the debt is still owed to him, even though the qabid collected his share in reality.
2
Analyze the rule on leaving collection and subsequent loss
If the non-possessing partner initially leaves the collected amount with the qabid (taslim) expecting the debtor to pay, but the debtor's remaining debt becomes lost, he can retroactively join in the collected amount. Reason: he only agreed to leave it in expectation of full recovery.
3
Understand muqassa and ibra
If there is a set-off (muqassa) or release (ibra) by a partner, the other partner cannot claim participation because set-off is discharge, not collection, and ibra is destruction (itlaf) of the right, not possession.
Key distinction: ibra is like destroying the right, while qabd is taking possession. Only qabd triggers participation rights.
4
Analyze the ta'khir dispute
If one partner defers (ta'khir) the debtor's payment for his share, Abu Yusuf holds it valid by analogy with ibra mutlaq. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) says invalid because it leads to division of debt before possession, as one part becomes deferred and the other immediate.
The relied-upon position is the majority view, as it prevents unequal treatment and maintains the indivisibility of the debt before qabd.

وَلِلشَّرِيكِ أَنْ يَتَّبِعَ الْغَرِيْمَ فِي جَمِيعِ مَا ذَكَرْنَا لِأَنَّ حَقَّهُ فِي ذِمَّتِهِ بَاقِ لِأَنَّ الْقَابِضَ اسْتَوْقَى نَصِيبَهُ حَقِيقَةً لَكِنَّ لَهُ حَقُّ الْمُشَارَكَةِ فَلَهُ أَنْ لَا يُشَارِكَهُ فَلَوْ سَلَّمَ لَهُ مَا قَبَضَ ثُمَّ تَوَى مَا عَلَى الْغَرِيْمِ لَهُ أَنْ يُشَارِكَ الْقَابِضَ لِأَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا رَضِيَ بِالتَّسْلِيمِ لِيُسَلَّمَ لَهُ مَا فِي ذِمَّةِ الْغَرِيمِ وَلَمْ يُسَلَّمَ وَلَوْ وَقَعَتِ الْمُقَاصَّةُ بِدَيْنٍ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ قَبْلِ لَمْ يَرْجِعُ عَلَيْهِ الشَرِيكَ لأَنَّهُ قَاضِ بِنَصِيبِهِ لَا مُقْتَضِ وَلَوْ اَبْرَاهُ عَنْ نَصِيبِهِ فَكَذَلِكَ لِأَنَّهُ إِثْلَاتٌ وَلَيْسَ بِقَبْضِ وَلَوْ إِبْرَاهِ عَنِ الْبَعْضِ كَانَتْ قِسْمَةُ الْبَاقِي عَلَى مَا بَقِيَ مِنَ السِّهَامِ وَلَوْ أَخَّرَ اَحَدُهُمَا عَنْ نَصِيبِهِ صَحَ عِنْدَ أَبِي وسُفَ اِعْتِبَارًا بِالْإِبْرَاءِ الْمُطْلَقِ وَلَا يَصِحُ عِنْدَهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ يُؤَدِى إِلَى قِسْمَةِ الدَّيْنِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ
ترجمہ اور غیر قابض شریک کو اختیار ہے کہ مدیون کا دامن گیر ہو۔ ان تمام صورتوں میں جو ہم نے ذکر کیں۔ کیونکہ اس کا حق اس کے ذمہ باقی ہے اس لئے کہ قابض نے در حقیقت اپنا حصہ وصول کیا ہے۔ لیکن اس کے لئے حق مشارکت ہے تو اس کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ مشارکت نہ کرے۔ پھر اگر شریک نے وصول کنندہ کو وہ سپر درکھا جو اس نے وصول کیا ہے اور جو مدیوں پر باقی تھا وہ ڈوب گیا تو اس کو اختیار ہے قابض کے ساتھ مشارکت کا۔ کیونکہ وہ سپر دکرنے پر اسی لئے راضی ہوا تھا تا کہ اس کو وہ ملے جو مدیون کے ذمہ ہے اور وہ اس کو نہیں ملا۔ اور اگر مقاصد اس دین سے ہوا جوکسی شریک پر پہلے سے تھا تو دوسرا شریک اس سے کچھ نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے حصہ سے قرض چکانے والا ہے وصول کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور اگر اپنے حصہ سے مدیون کو بری کر دیا تب بھی یوں ہی ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ اختلاف ہے نہ کہ قبضہ۔ اور اگر بعض حصہ سے بری کیا تو باقی قرضہ کی تقسیم باقی ماندہ حق کے موافق حقہ رسد ہوگی ۔ اور اگر کسی شریک نے مدیون کو اپنے حصہ کی مہلت دے دی تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک صحیح ہے ابراء مطلق پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور طرفین کے نزدیک صحیح نہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ قبضہ سے پہلے قرضہ کے ہزارہ کی طرف مفضی ہے
قوله وللشريك ان يتبع - غير قابض شریک کو مذکورہ تمام صورتوں میں یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ قرض دار کا دامن گیر ہو کر اپنا حق وصول کرے۔ کیونکہ ابھی اس کا حق قرضدار کے ذمہ باقی ہے اس لئے کہ وصول کنندہ شریک نے در حقیقت اپنا حصہ وصول کیا ہے۔ لیکن اس کو شریک قابض کے ساتھ مشارکت کا حق ہے تو اس کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ مشارکت نہ کرے۔ ....... قوله فلوسلم له ما قبض ... الخ - پھر اگر شریک نے وصول کی ہے یعنی اس سے بنوارہ نہیں کیا۔ پھر جو کچھ مدیون کے ذمہ باقی تھا۔ وہ ڈوب گیا۔ مثلا وہ مفلس ہو کر مر گیا تو اس کو اختیار ہوگا کہ وہ مقبوض مقدار میں دوسرے شریک کا سا بھی ہو جائے۔ اس لئے کہ وہ مسلم رکھنے پر اسی لئے راضی ہوا تھا کہ جو کچھ مدیون پر باقی ہے وہ اس کو ملے اور جب وہ اس کو نہیں ملا تو اس کو شرکت کا اختیار ہوگا۔
قوله ولو وقعت القاصة .... الخ - اگر مسئلہ مذکورہ میں یہ صورت ہو کہ مدیون کا کچھ قرضہ پہلے ہی سے شریکین میں سے کسی شریک کے ذمہ تھا۔ پس اس قرضہ سے شریک کے حصہ کا بدلا ہو گیا تو دوسرا شریک اپنے شریک سے کچھ واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے حصہ سے مدیون کا قرضہ چکانے والا ہوا نہ کہ اپنا حصہ قرض وصول کرنے والا۔ اور اگر ایک شریک نے اپنے حصہ سے مدیون کو بری کر دیا تب بھی دوسرا شریک اس سے کچھ واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ ابراء اتلاف ہے نہ کہ قبضہ ۔
قوله ولو ابـراه عن البعض .... الخ - اگر شریک نے مدیون کو اپنے کچھ حصہ سے بری کیا تو باقی قرضہ کی تقسیم باقی ماندہ حق کے موافق حصہ رسد ہوگی۔ مثلاً سوروپیہ قرض میں سے ایک شریک نے اپنا نصف حصہ معاف کیا تو کل قرضہ کا چہارم نکل جانے کے بعد کچھتر روپیہ دونوں میں اس طرح مشترک ہوگا کہ ایک حصہ معاف کرنے والے کا ہوگا اور دو حصے دوسرے شریک کے ہوں گے اور اگر کچھ حصہ وصول کر لیا گیا تب بھی وہ ان میں حصہ کے موافق مشترک ہوگا۔
قوله ولو اخر احد هما ... الخ - اگر شریکین میں سے ایک نے اپنے حصہ میں مدیون کو مہلت دے دی۔ تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ابراء مطلق پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ یہ تاخیر و تاجیل صحیح ہوگی۔ اور طرفین کے نزدیک صحیح نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ یہ قبضہ سے پہلے قرضہ کے بٹوارہ دوستلزم ہے اس لئے کہ ایک شریک کا حصہ میعادی ہو گیا۔ جس کا مطالبہ بالفعل نہیں ہوسکتا اور دوسرے کا حصہ غیر میعادی رہا۔ جس کا مطالبہ فی الحال ہوسکتا ہے۔
The partner has the right to pursue the debtor in all that we have mentioned, because his right remains in the debtor's liability. Indeed, the receiving partner actually received his share, but he has the right of participation, so he may choose not to participate with him. Then if he (the non-possessing partner) left what he (the possessing partner) had received for him, and then what was owed by the debtor was lost, he has the right to participate with the receiver, because he only agreed to the surrender so that what was in the debtor's liability would be secured for him, but it was not secured. And if set-off (muqassa) occurred with a debt that was previously owed by him (the partner), the other partner does not have recourse against him, because he is discharging his share, not receiving. And if he released the debtor from his share, it is likewise, because it is destruction (itlaf), not possession (qabd). And if he released from part, then the division of the remaining debt is according to the remaining shares. And if one of them deferred his share, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf, by analogy with absolute release (ibra mutlaq), but it is not valid according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), because it leads to division of debt before possession.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Sulh addresses the rights of partners in a shared debt where one partner has already collected from the debtor. The passage type is a ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute. The non-possessing partner retains the right to pursue the debtor for his share. Even if the possessing partner took physical possession of the debtor's property (whether cash or goods) and used it as his share, the non-possessing partner still has a claim against the debtor. However, he also has the option to participate in what the possessing partner collected. If he initially leaves what was collected with the possessing partner (meaning he does not demand participation), but later the debtor's remaining debt becomes lost (e.g., the debtor dies insolvent), he may then choose to participate in what was collected, because he only left it with the expectation that the debtor would pay. If set-off (muqassa) occurs—meaning the possessing partner had a prior debt from the debtor and used it to offset his share—the non-possessing partner cannot recover from his partner because the partner was merely discharging his debt, not collecting. Similarly, if the partner releases the debtor from his share (ibra), it is considered destruction (itlaf), not possession, so no participation. If only part is released, the remaining debt is divided proportionally among the original shares. Regarding deferment (ta'khir): if one partner gives the debtor more time to pay his share, Imam Abu Yusuf considers it valid by analogy with outright release, because the partner waives his right to immediate payment. However, Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad consider it invalid because it effectively divides the debt before possession, as one part becomes deferred while the other remains due immediately, leading to an uneven split. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the view of the two (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad), as stated in the commentary.

Key Terms
مشارکت (mushārakah): The right of a non-possessing partner to share in what the possessing partner has collected from the common debtor.
اقتضاء (iqtiḍā): Legal implication or requirement; here, the act of collecting from the debtor.
ابراء (ibrāʾ): Release from debt; considered itlaf (destruction) of the right, not qabd (possession).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), is a partner's deferment of the debtor's payment for his share valid?
A) Yes, valid by analogy with ibra mutlaq
B) No, invalid because it leads to division of debt before possession
C) Yes, valid if both partners agree
D) No, invalid because the debtor does not consent

Key Takeaway
The non-possessing partner has a right to participate in collected amounts if the debtor's remaining debt is lost, but release (ibra) destroys that right; deferment (ta'khir) is invalid according to the majority because it effectively divides the debt before possession.

Actions Constituting Possession (Qabd) in Partnership Debt: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Burning
Lists actions constituting constructive possession (qabd) of a partner's share, with an intra-Hanafi dispute on burning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which actions constitute constructive possession (qabd) of a partner's share and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on burning (ihraq).

Core Idea
In partnership debt, certain acts like ghasb, corrupt sale, hiring, and settlement are qabd; burning is disputed between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines various actions a partner may take with the debtor's assets and whether they constitute possession (qabd) of his share, thereby extinguishing the debtor's liability. Understanding this is crucial for determining when a partner's right is realized and when the other partners can still pursue the debtor. The text presents the majority position and highlights an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding burning.

Guided Path
1
Identify Actions Considered Qabd
The passage lists several acts that are explicitly considered qabd: wrongful taking (ghasb), corrupt purchase (shira fasid) with subsequent loss, hiring (isti'jar), and settlement (sulh) for intentional injury. Also note that marriage (tazawwuj) is explicitly said to be itlaf, not qabd.
These are the agreed positions in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Recognize the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Burning
Regarding burning (ihraq), the text states it is qabd according to Imam Muhammad, but not according to Imam Abu Yusuf. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
The disagreement centers on whether destruction with intent to take constitutes possession.
3
Examine the Rationale (Talil) for Each Position
Muhammad's view: The partner's act of burning effectively takes the property by destroying it for his own benefit, so it functions as qabd. Abu Yusuf's view: Burning is pure destruction (itlaf), not a taking; therefore it cannot be qabd.
The underlying principle is whether the partner has 'taken control' (tasarruf) over the share.
4
Analyse the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
If qabd is established, the debtor's liability for that share is extinguished, and the other partner cannot claim it. If not qabd, the debtor remains liable to the other partner.
This directly affects the rights of co-partners and creditors.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
According to the commentary, many later Hanafi scholars prefer Muhammad's view on burning, making it the operative position for fatwa.
The tarjih authority is the commentator (likely Ibn Abidin or Marghinani in his commentary).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ غَصَبَ اَحَدُهُمَا عَيْنًا مِنْهُ أَوِ اشْتَرَاهُ شِرَاءً فَاسِدًا وَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ فَهُوَ قَبْضٌ وَالْإِسْتِيْجَارُ بِنَصِيبِهِ قَبْضٌ وَكَذَا الْإِحْرَاقُ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ خِلَافًا لَابِى يُوسُفَ وَالتَّزَوُّجُ بِهِ اِثْلَاثِ فِى ظَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَةِ وَكَذَا الصُّلْحُ عَلَيْهِ عَنْ جِنَايَةِ الْعَمَدِ
قوله ولو غصب احدهما .... الخ - اگر ایک شریک نے مدیون کی ایسی چیز غصب کرلی جس کی قیمت اس کے حصہ قرض کے برابر ہے یا اس سے بطریق فاسد کوئی چیز خرید لی۔ اور وہ اس تحریک کے قبضہ میں تلف ہوگئی تو یہ اپنے حصہ اک قرضہ کا قبضہ ہو گیا اور اگر اپنے حصہ کے عوض کوئی چیز اجارہ پر لے لی۔ مثلاً ایک شخص کے ذمہ دو شریکوں کے ایک ہزار درہم تھے۔ پس ایک شریک نے اپنے حصہ کے پانچ سو کے عوض مدیون سے ایک مکان ایک سال تک رہنے کے لئے اجارہ پر لے لیا اور اس میں ایک سال رہ لیا تو یہ بھی اپنے حصہ کا قبضہ ہو گیا۔ اسی طرح مدیون کی کوئی چیز جلا دینا بھی امام محمد کے نزدیک قبضہ ہے برخلاف امام ابو یوسف کے بقول بعض اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ شریک نے آگ کا انگارہ پھینکا جس سے مدیون کا کپڑا جل گیا۔ اور اگر کپڑا لے کر بالقصد جلا دیا تو بالاتفاق ضامن ہوگا۔
And if one of them wrongfully takes (ghasb) an item from him (the debtor), or buys it through a corrupt sale (shira fasid) and it perishes in his hand, it is possession (qabd). And hiring (isti'jar) for his share is possession. Likewise, burning (ihraq) according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. And marrying (tazawwuj) with it is destruction (itlaf) in Zahir al-Riwayah. Likewise, settlement (sulh) upon it for intentional injury (jinayat al-amd).
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of partnership in debt, specifically what actions by a partner constitute constructive possession (qabd) of his share. The passage type is a ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute. The general rule: if a partner takes an asset from the debtor by wrongful appropriation (ghasb) or through a defective purchase (shira fasid) and the asset perishes in his hands, this is considered possession of his share. Similarly, hiring (isti'jar) the debtor's property in exchange for his share is also possession. Regarding burning (ihraq): Imam Muhammad holds that if the partner throws a burning ember that destroys the debtor's property, it counts as possession. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, considering it destruction, not possession. However, if the partner intentionally takes and burns the property, all agree he is liable (damin). Marriage (tazawwuj): if a partner marries the debtor's female relative or the debtor himself? The text says 'tazawwuj bihi' – marrying with it – likely meaning he uses his share as dower (mahr) to marry someone. This is considered destruction (itlaf), not possession, in Zahir al-Riwayah. Settlement (sulh): if a partner settles his share in exchange for forgiveness from an intentional injury (jinayat al-amd) owed by the debtor, that also counts as possession.

Key Terms
قبض (qabḍ): Possession that establishes the partner's right over the debtor's asset, extinguishing the debtor's liability for that share.
إتلاف (itlāf): Destruction of the asset; in the case of tazawwuj, it is considered itlaf, not qabd.
صلح (ṣulḥ): Settlement; here, a partner settling his share in exchange for forgiveness of an intentional injury (jinayat al-amd) is deemed qabd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, which of the following actions is considered possession (qabd) of a partner's share from the debtor?
A) Marrying (tazawwuj) with the share
B) Burning (ihraq) the debtor's property
C) Setting off a prior debt (muqassa)
D) Releasing (ibra) the debtor

Key Takeaway
In partnership debt, possession (qabd) can be established through various acts including ghasb, shira fasid, isti'jar, and sulh; tazawwuj is itlaf; burning (ihraq) is qabd according to Imam Muhammad, which is the mufta bihi view.

Settlement in Salam Between Partners: Abu Hanifa's Ruling
Ruling statement with implied ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Abu Hanifa regarding a partner settling with the salam capital, and explain why it is invalid.

Core Idea
Settlement with the salam capital is invalid because it amounts to selling debt for debt.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in salam contracts where two partners jointly pay the capital. If one partner attempts to settle with the seller by taking back his share of the capital, Abu Hanifa rules that such settlement is invalid. The reasoning stems from the nature of the capital as a debt that cannot be reassigned before delivery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
What is the situation? Two partners jointly advance capital in a salam contract. One partner wishes to settle with the seller by taking back his share of the capital.
2
State the ruling
According to Abu Hanifa, the settlement is invalid (lam yajuz).
3
Understand the rationale
Once paid, the salam capital becomes a debt owed by the seller. Settling with the capital would be like selling a debt for a debt, which is prohibited in Hanafi fiqh.
The key principle: ra's al-mal in salam becomes a dayn (debt).
4
Recognize the ikhtilaf
The text introduces this with 'اقوال فقہاء' implying there are other views, likely from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سلم کا مال دوشریکوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو ایک نے اپنے حصے کے راس المال سے صلح کر لی صلح جائز ہے یا نہیں؟ ، اقوال فقہاء قَالَ وَإِذَا كَانَ السَّلَمُ بَيْنَ شَرِيكَيْنِ فَصَالَحَ أَحَدُهُمَا عَنْ نَصِيبِهِ عَلَى رَأسِ الْمَالِ لَمْ يَجُزْ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ
The capital of salam (advance payment) is shared between two partners. One of them made a settlement (sulh) for his share with the capital. Is the settlement valid? Statements of jurists. He (the author) said: When the salam is between two partners, and one of them settles for his share with the capital, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage introduces a new sub-topic: salam (advance sale) where partners have jointly paid capital to the seller for future delivery of goods. One partner wishes to settle with the seller by taking back his share of the capital (i.e., cancel his participation). The passage type is a ruling statement with a brief mention of ikhtilaf (implied, as only Abu Hanifa's view is given). According to Abu Hanifa, such a settlement is invalid because salam capital is like a debt that cannot be sold back before possession. The commentary likely continues with views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but the OCR cuts off. The ruling is that the partner cannot simply take back his capital through sulh; the salam contract remains binding.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): An advance sale where the buyer pays the price (ra's al-mal) immediately for future delivery of specified goods.
رأس المال (raʾs al-māl): The capital paid in advance in a salam contract.
صلح (ṣulḥ): A settlement or compromise, often involving a transaction to resolve a dispute or cancel an obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid (ja'iz)
B) Invalid (la yajuz)
C) Valid only with the seller's consent
D) Valid if the other partner agrees

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa rules that a partner in a salam contract cannot settle with the capital because the capital becomes a debt, and settling with it would be selling debt for debt.

Settlement by One Partner in a Joint Salam Contract: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of sulh in joint salam contract, with proofs and condition on mixing capital.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the validity of sulh by one partner in a joint salam contract, explain the proofs of each side, and apply the condition regarding mixing of capital.

Core Idea
A partner cannot unilaterally settle his share of a joint salam debt; the contract is indivisible until receipt.

When two partners jointly provide the capital for a salam contract, can one partner separately settle his share with the seller? This question divides the Hanafi school. In this lesson, you will analyze the arguments of the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and the minority view of Abu Yusuf, and understand the crucial condition about whether the capitals were mixed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Determine the exact scenario: two partners jointly pay the capital (ra's al-mal) in a salam contract. One partner makes a sulh (compromise) with the seller regarding his share of the capital. What is the ruling on this sulh?
The dispute is about validity, not about the permissibility of sulh in general.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and his proof (qiyas)
Abu Yusuf holds that the sulh is valid. His proof is qiyas: (1) analogy to other debts where a partner can settle his share, and (2) analogy to a joint purchase of a tangible object where one partner can cancel (iqalah) his share.
Note that both analogies treat the salam debt as similar to other debts or tangible goods.
3
State the majority position and their two arguments
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule it invalid. They give two grounds: (1) if the sulh is limited to the partner's share, it amounts to dividing a debt before receipt (which is invalid); (2) if the sulh affects both shares, the other partner must consent, and even if allowed, the other partner would share in the received amount, leading to the revival of the salam after its lapse.
The first argument focuses on debt indivisibility; the second on the risk of reviving a lapsed obligation.
4
Apply the condition of mixing capital
The text adds: the above dispute applies when the two partners mixed their capitals. If they did not mix, then according to the first argument the dispute remains, but according to the second argument there is agreement on invalidity because the other partner has no share in the received amount.
This limits the scope of disagreement.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the sulh is invalid, especially when the capital is mixed. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
The tarjih is based on consistency with principles and majority weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمُحَمَّدٌ وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ يَجُوزُ الصُّلْحُ اِعْتِبَارًا بِسَائِرِ الدُّيُون وَبِمَا إِذَا اشْتَرَيَا عَبْدًا فَاقَالَ اَحَدُهُمَا فِى نَـ [؟] وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ لَوْ جَازَ فِى نَصِيبِهِ خَاصَّةً يَكُونُ قِسْمَةُ الدَّيْنِ فِي الذِمَّةِ وَلَوْ جَازَ فِى نَصِيبِهِمَا لَابُدَّ مِنْ إِجَازَةِ الْآخَرَ بِخِلَافِ شِرَى الْعَيْنِ وَهَذَا لِاَنَّ الْمُسْلَم فِيْهِ صَارَ وَاجِبًا بِالْعَقْدِ وَالْعَقْدُ قَامَ بِهِمَا فَلَا يَتَفَرَّدُ اَحَدُهُمَا بِرَفْعِهِ وَ لأَنَّهُ لَوْ جَازَ لَشَارَكَه فِي الْمَقْبُوضِ فَإِذَا شَارَكَهُ فِيْهِ رَجَعَ الْمَصَالِحُ عَلَى مَنْ عَلَيْهِ بِذلِكَ فَيُؤَدِّي إِلَى عَوْدِ السَّلَم بَعْدَ سُقُوطِهِ قَالُوا هَذَا إِذَا خَلَطَا رَأسَ الْمَالِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُونَا قَدْ خَلَطَاهُ فَعَلَى الْوَجْهِ الْأَوَّلِ هُوَ عَلَى الْخِلَافِ وَعَلَى وَجْهِ الثَّانِي هُوَ عَلَى الْإِتِفَاقِ
And Muhammad (said it is invalid). Abu Yusuf said: The sulh is permissible by analogy to other debts and to the case where they bought a slave and one of them cancels (the sale) in his share. Their argument (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that if it were allowed specifically in his share, it would be a division of a debt in the dhimmah, and if allowed in both their shares, the other's permission is necessary, unlike the purchase of a tangible good. This is because the muslam fīh becomes obligatory by the contract, and the contract stands with both of them, so one of them cannot alone remove it. And also because if it were allowed, the other would share in what is received, and when he shares in it, the benefit returns to the one against whom it is (the debt), leading to the return of the salam after its lapse. They said: This is when they mixed the capital. If they had not mixed it, then according to the first aspect it is based on the disagreement, and according to the second aspect it is based on agreement.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a sulh (compromise) made by one partner in a salam contract where the capital (ra's al-mal) was jointly provided. The ruling: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the majority of the school), such a sulh is invalid. Abu Yusuf holds it is valid. The Hanafi authority weight: This is from Zahir al-Riwayah as reported in Al-Hidayah and similar texts. The basis of Abu Yusuf's opinion is qiyas (analogy) to two scenarios: (1) other debts where one partner can settle his share individually, and (2) the purchase of a tangible object (ayn) where one partner can cancel (iqalah) his share. The response of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the majority) is twofold. First, if the sulh is limited to the partner's share only, it necessitates a division of a debt before receipt (qabd), which is invalid. If it affects both shares, the other partner's consent is required, which is absent. Unlike the purchase of a tangible good where the contract is complete and one partner can cancel, in salam the muslam fīh is a debt that becomes obligatory by the contract, and the contract is established with both parties; one cannot unilaterally annul it. Second, if the sulh were valid, the other partner would share in the amount received (since the contract is one), and the partner making sulh would then recover that amount from the muslam ilayh, causing the salam to revive after being dropped, which is invalid. The later scholars (mutakhkhirin) added a condition: this dispute applies when the two partners mixed their capitals. If they did not mix, then according to the first argument (division of debt) the dispute remains, but according to the second argument (sharing in receipt) there is agreement on invalidity because the other partner has no share in the received amount.

Key Terms
السلم (al-salam): A sale with advance payment for future delivery of specified goods.
المسلم فيه (al-muslam fīhi): The subject matter of salam, which is a debt obligation on the seller.
الصُلْح (al-sulh): A compromise or settlement whereby a claimant accepts something in lieu of his claim, often terminating the original obligation.
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital paid in advance by the buyer in a salam contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why is the sulh by one partner in a joint salam contract invalid?
A) Because the partner lacks legal capacity to make sulh.
B) Because it would require division of a debt before receipt, which is invalid.
C) Because the other partner did not give consent at the time of contract.
D) Because the muslam fīhi is a tangible object that cannot be divided.

Key Takeaway
In a joint salam, the contract is indivisible; a partner cannot unilaterally settle his share of the capital without the other's consent, as it would divide a debt not yet received or risk reviving a lapsed obligation.

One Partner's Sulh in Salam: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute over partner's individual sulh in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two sides) and of Abu Yusuf regarding one partner's sulh in a salam contract, and explain the reasoning and the effect of capital mixing.

Core Idea
A partner's individual sulh in salam is invalid according to the two sides; Abu Yusuf permits it, with the dispute hinging on capital mixing.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether one partner in a salam contract can individually settle with the muslam ilayh. The two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue invalidity based on the joint nature of the contract and the legal consequences of reviving a terminated contract. Abu Yusuf disagrees. Later scholars qualified the dispute based on whether the partners mixed their capital. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the thamarah al-khilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their positions
Recognize that the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold the sulh invalid, while Abu Yusuf holds it permissible.
The two sides are sometimes called 'tarafayn' in the text.
2
Understand the first reason of the two sides
The contract is joint; one partner cannot unilaterally annul it because the debt is established for both jointly.
This reason applies regardless of capital mixing.
3
Understand the second reason
If the sulh were valid, the partner who takes payment would share it with the other partner. Then he would return the muslam fih to the debtor, effectively reviving the contract after its termination, which is invalid.
This reason only applies when capital is mixed.
4
Analyze the qualification of later scholars
When capital is mixed, both reasons apply; when not mixed, only the first reason applies, but the dispute remains.
The second reason is neutralized because there is no partnership in the received amount.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a partner makes a sulh, according to the two sides it is invalid, so the other partner can claim his share; according to Abu Yusuf it is valid.
The later scholars' qualification does not change the dispute's existence.

The reason for the mentioned difference is that the debt is the muslam fih (subject matter), so it is established as obligatory due to the contract, and the contract stands with both partners, so neither has the authority to annul the contract. (He said: And because if it were permissible... - The second proof of the two sides is that if the mentioned sulh were permissible, then the partner making sulh would share with the other partner whatever he received from the capital, because it is a single transaction and their partnership is established. Then when he takes his share as a partner, he would take back from the muslam ilayh (the debtor) the muslam fih (subject matter) equal to what he received, while the debt still exists, because now half the muslam fih remains due from the muslam ilayh, even though he had terminated the salam contract by the sulh. So after the salam contract falls, its return becomes necessary and this is invalid. (He said: They said this when they mixed... - The later scholars said that the mentioned dispute is when both partners mixed their capital and made the salam contract. But if they did not mix, rather each gave his capital separately, then according to the first proof, this also falls under the same dispute: in the view of the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), one partner's sulh is not permissible because if this sulh is only permissible in his share, then the division of the debt before taking possession becomes necessary, which is not permissible. And according to Abu Yusuf, the sulh is permissible. And according to the second proof, the sulh is unanimously permissible, because when each gave capital separately, there is no partnership between them in it. Hence the receiving partner has no share with the partner making sulh, because that wealth is solely his right. Benefit... In al-Kifayah it says: The correct view is that whether the capital is mixed or not, in any case the dispute is established. The only difference is that in the case of mixing, the invalidity in the view of the two sides is for both reasons, and in the case of no mixing, the invalidity is only for one reason, i.e., the second reason that the other partner has no right to share in what was taken. Then in Sharh al-'Inayah it says: Does the dispute occur only when the capital is mixed or absolutely? The basis of the difference among the later scholars is that Imam Muhammad mentioned the dispute with mixing in Kitab al-Buyu', and in Kitab al-Sulh he stated clearly without mixing that according to Abu Yusuf the other partner will not share in the quantity taken by the partner making sulh, and he did not mention the statement of the two sides. Some understood from this omission that there is agreement in that case.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of one partner in a salam contract making a sulh (compromise) with the muslam ilayh (debtor) without the other partner's consent. The text presents two reasons (dalil) from the side of the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) for considering the sulh invalid. First reason: The debt is established by the contract for both partners jointly, so one cannot unilaterally annul it. Second reason: If such sulh were allowed, the partner taking the payment would share it with the other partner because the contract is a single unit (safqah wahidah); then he would take back the muslam fih from the muslam ilayh, effectively reviving the contract after its termination, which is invalid. Then the text addresses a qualification from later scholars: this dispute applies when the partners mixed their capital. If they did not mix, then the first reason still applies (dispute remains), but the second reason does not apply because there is no partnership in the received amount. According to the second reason, the sulh would be permissible by consensus. Finally, the passage records a difference among later scholars about whether the dispute is only in mixed capital or absolutely, citing Imam Muhammad's different treatments in al-Buyu' and al-Sulh. The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but the text leans toward the position of the two sides (invalidity).

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A compromise or settlement where the muslam ilayh gives something to the partner in lieu of the debt.
خلط رأس المال (khald ra's al-mal): Mixing the capital of two partners together before making the salam contract.
مسلم فيہ (muslam fih): The subject matter of the salam contract, e.g., a commodity to be delivered.

C) Valid, because Abu Yusuf allows it.
D) Invalid, because of the second reason only.

Key Takeaway
The two sides hold that one partner's sulh in salam is invalid whether capital is mixed or not, while Abu Yusuf permits it; the Hanafi mufta bihi is the two sides' view.

Sulh with Silver and Gold: Equality and Possession Conditions
Ruling on sulh with unequal exchange of silver for gold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid sulh when the estate and settlement are of different ribawi metals, and distinguish when prior possession suffices based on qabḍ ḍamān vs. qabḍ amānah.

Core Idea
In sulh exchanging gold for silver, equality of weight is not required, but hand-to-hand possession in the session is mandatory.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in Hanafi fiqh concerning sulh (compromise settlement) in inheritance when the estate consists entirely of one type of currency (silver or gold) and the settling heir receives the other type. The passage clarifies that because gold and silver are different genera for riba purposes, the settlement is treated as a currency exchange (ṣarf) with specific possession requirements. Additionally, the text explores how the nature of the heir's prior possession (guarantee vs. trust) affects whether a new possession must take place in the session.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act is sulh (compromise) in inheritance, where the estate is entirely one metal (silver or gold) and the settlement is in the other metal. This falls under bay‘ ṣarf (currency exchange) because different genera are exchanged.
Sulh here is a sale, so rules of ṣarf apply.
2
Determine the hukm level and conditions
Sulh is mubah (permissible) in itself, but for validity, hand-to-hand possession (taqābuḍ) in the session is wajib. Equality of weight is not required because gold and silver are different genera.
The passage states: 'equality is not considered, but hand-to-hand exchange in the session is considered'.
3
Analyze the possession requirement for the heir holding the remainder
If the heir who holds the remainder of the estate denies possession, his existing possession is qabḍ ḍamān (possession of guarantee), which suffices for the sulh. If he acknowledges possession, it is qabḍ amānah (possession of trust), which does not substitute; a new possession in the session is required.
Denial turns trust possession into guarantee possession.
4
Extract the general principle of possession substitution
The commentary states: guarantee possession can substitute for trust possession, but not vice versa. This is a broader rule applicable in similar contexts.
This principle guides when a pre-existing possession can fulfill the possession requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِنْ كَانَتِ السَّرْكَةُ فِضَّةٌ فَاعْطُوهُ ذَهَبًا أَوْ كَانَ ذَهَبًا فَاعْطُوهُ فِضَّةٌ فَكَذلِكَ لأَنَّهُ بَيْعُ الْجنس بِخِلَافِ الجنسِ فَلَا يُعتبر السَّسَاوِى وَيُعتبر الْتَقَابُضُ فِى الْمَجْلِسِ لأَنَّهُ صَرْت غَيْرَ أَنَّ الَّذِي فِي يَدِهِ بَقِيَّةِ التَّرْكَةِ إِنْ كَانَ جَاحِدًا يُكْتَفِى بِذلِكَ الْقَبْضُ لأنَّهُ قَبضُ ضَمَانِ فَيَنُوبُ عَنْ قَبْضِ الصُّلْحِ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُقَرًّا لَابُدَّ مِنْ تَجْدِيدِ الْقَبْضِ لِأَنَّهُ قَبْضُ أَمَانَةٍ فَلَا يَتُوبُ عَنْ قَبْضِ الصُّلْحِ
ترجمہ اور اگر ترکہ چاندی ہو اور سونا دین یا سونا ہواور وہ چاندی دیں تب بھی یوں ہی ہے کیونکہ یہ ایک جنس کی بیج ہے خلاف جنس سے تو برابری معتبر نہ ہوگی اور مجلس میں قبضہ ہوجانا معتبر ہوگا کیونکہ یہ بیع صرف ہے۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ جس کے قبضہ میں باقی ترکہ ہے اگر وہ منکر ہو تو اس قبضہ پر اکتفاء کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ ضمانتی قبضہ ہے تو قبضہ صلح کا نائب ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر وہ مقر ہو تو جدید قبضہ ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ قبضہ امانت ہے تو قبضہ صلح کا نائب نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح قوله وان كانت التركة فضة..... الخ اگر میت کے ترکہ میں چاندی ہو او ورثے اس کے عوض سونا دیں یا ترکہ میں سونا ہوا۔ اور وہ عوض میں چاندی دیں تب بھی یہی حکم ہے کہ عوض قلیل ہو یا کثیر سب جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ایک جنس کو اس کے خلاف جس کے اس میں مساوات معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ البتہ اس مجلس میں قبضہ ہو جانا شرط ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بیچ صرف ہے۔ اور بیچ صرف میں نقابض شرط ہے۔ لیکن اتنی بات ہے کہ جس وارث کے قبضہ میں باقی ترکہ ہے۔ اگر وہ اس امر سے منکر ہو کہ ترکہ اس کے قبضہ میں ہے تو اس قبضہ سابقہ پر اکتفاء کیا جائے گا۔ اور جدید قبضہ کی ضرورت نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس کے انکار کی وجہ سے اس کا قبضہ ضمانتی قبضہ ہے۔ یعنی وہ انکار کی وجہ سے مال کا ضامن ہو گیا تو صلح کی وجہ سے جو قبضہ لازم آیا ہے اس کے بجائے اس کا موجود قبضہ کافی ہوگا اور اگر وہ وارث جس کے قبضہ میں باقی ترکہ ہے وہ قبضہ امانت ہے جو قبضہ صلح کا نائب نہیں ہوسکتا۔ اور قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ جب قبضے امانت یا ضمانت کے لحاظ سے متجانس ہوں تو ان میں سے ایک دوسرے کا نائب ہو جاتا ہے اور اگر متجانس نہ ہوں مختلف ہوں تو ضمانتی قبضہ قبضہ امانت کا نائب ہو سکتا ہے اس کا عکس نہیں ہوسکتا۔
He said: And if the estate is silver and they give him gold, or it was gold and they give him silver, then similar; because it is a sale of one genus for a different genus, so equality is not considered, but hand-to-hand exchange in the session is considered because it is a currency exchange (ṣarf). Except that the one in whose hand is the remainder of the estate: if he is a denier, that possession suffices because it is a possession of guarantee (qabḍ damān), so it substitutes for the possession of sulh; and if he is an acknowledger, renewal of possession is necessary because it is a possession of trust (qabḍ amānah), so it does not substitute for the possession of sulh. Translation: And if the estate is silver and they give gold, or it is gold and they give silver, then the same applies: because it is a sale of one genus for a different genus, so equality is not considered, and possession in the session is considered because it is a currency exchange. The only thing is that the one in whose hand is the remainder of the estate: if he denies, that possession suffices because it is a possession of guarantee, so it becomes a substitute for the possession of sulh. And if he acknowledges, renewal of possession is necessary because it is a possession of trust, so it does not substitute for the possession of sulh. Commentary: His statement: 'and if the estate is silver...' etc. If the deceased's estate contains silver and the heirs give gold in exchange, or the estate contains gold and they give silver in exchange, then the same ruling applies: whether the consideration is little or much, it is all permissible. Because it is a sale of one genus for another genus, so equality is not considered. However, possession in that session is a condition because it is a currency exchange, and in currency exchange, possession is a condition. But the point is: the heir in whose hand is the remainder of the estate: if he denies that the estate is in his possession, then that prior possession suffices, and a new possession is not needed. Because due to his denial, his possession is a possession of guarantee; i.e., he became a guarantor of the property due to denial, so his existing possession is sufficient instead of the possession required by sulh. And if the heir in whose hand is the remainder of the estate acknowledges, then that possession is a possession of trust, which cannot substitute for the possession of sulh. And the general principle is: when possessions are homogeneous in terms of trust or guarantee, then one substitutes for the other; and if they are not homogeneous but different, then the possession of guarantee can substitute for the possession of trust, but not vice versa.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with commentary from the matn and sharh. It deals with sulh (compromise) in inheritance when the estate consists entirely of one monetary type (silver or gold) and the settlement is in the other type. Since gold and silver are different genera for riba purposes, equality of amount is not required; however, hand-to-hand exchange (taqābuḍ) in the session is obligatory because it is a ṣarf (currency exchange) contract. The commentary then addresses a nuance: if the heir who holds the remainder of the estate denies possession, his existing possession (which is now a guarantee possession due to his denial) suffices for the sulh. If he admits possession, his possession is a trust possession, which does not substitute for the sulh possession, so a new possession must take place in the session. The general rule is that guarantee possession can suffice for trust possession but not the reverse.

Key Terms
قبض ضمان (qabḍ ḍamān): Possession that makes the possessor liable for the property, e.g., due to denial of trust; this type of possession suffices for sulh.
قبض امانت (qabḍ amānah): Possession as a trustee; does not substitute for possession required in sulh/ṣarf.
بیع صرف (bay‘ ṣarf): Exchange of gold for silver or vice versa; requires hand-to-hand possession (taqābuḍ) in the session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sulh where the estate is silver and the settlement is gold, what condition is required to avoid riba?
A) Exact equality of weight
B) Hand-to-hand possession in the session
C) Written contract
D) Witnesses

Key Takeaway
When the sulh involves different ribawi genera, equality is not required, but hand-to-hand possession in the session is mandatory; the nature of prior possession (guarantee vs. trust) determines whether a new possession is needed.

Sulh with Mixed Estate: Avoiding Riba and the Ibrā' Alternative
Ruling on sulh with mixed estate: must exceed heir's share of same genus to avoid riba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a valid sulh in a mixed estate (must exceed heir's share of same genus) and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute over considering it as ibrā'.

Core Idea
In sulh with mixed estate, prevent riba by giving excess over same genus; a later view accepts ibrā' from claim as alternative.

This passage examines a specific inheritance settlement (takhāruj) where the estate contains gold, silver, and goods. The heirs wish to give one heir only gold or silver to exit the estate. The main rule is straightforward: the amount given must exceed the heir's share of that genus to avoid riba. However, a later Hanafi master, Ṣāḥib al-Natā'ij, questions whether this arrangement can be considered a release (ibrā') rather than an exchange, which would relax the conditions. This lesson unpacks the conditions and the refinement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the core condition
Recognize that this is a sulh (takhāruj) in a mixed estate. The amount of gold or silver given must be more than the heir's share of that genus. This ensures the heir gets his share plus extra for other goods.
The condition applies only when the sulh is in the same genus as part of the estate.
2
Explain the riba mechanism
If the amount is equal or less, part of the heir's share of that genus goes uncompensated, resulting in riba al-fadl. The excess compensates for other goods.
This is analogous to exchanging different genera; the excess is effectively payment for other goods.
3
Introduce the ibrā' alternative
The commentary raises the question: can this be considered ibrā' (release) so the heir gives up rights to the remainder? The initial answer is no, because ibrā' from tangible property (ʿayn) is invalid.
Ibrā' applies to debts, not to physical assets in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Analyze the critical refinement
Ṣāḥib al-Natā'ij argues that ibrā' from the claim to ʿayn is valid, and since the heir's speech should be interpreted favorably, the sulh can be valid as ibrā'.
This is a later refinement and is considered acceptable by some authorities.
5
Resolve with Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and the final ruling
The relied-upon position (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah) is that the sulh is valid with the condition of excess. The ibrā' view is a permissible refinement, especially when it helps uphold contracts.
In practice, both methods may be used, but the condition of excess and taqābuḍ for ṣarf remain important.

وَإِنْ كَانَتِ التَّرْكَةُ ذَهَبًا وَفِضَّةَ وَغَيْرَ ذَلِكَ فَصَالَحُوْهُ عَلَى فِضَّةٍ أَوْ ذَهَبٍ فَلَابُدَّ أنْ يَكُونَ مَا أَعْطُوهُ اَكْثَرَ مِنْ نَصِيبِهِ مِنْ ذلِكَ الْجِنْسِ حَتَّى يَكُونَ نَصِيبُهُ بِمِثْلِهِ وَالزِّيَادَةُ لِحَقِّهِ مِنْ بَقِيَّةِ التَّرْكَةِ اِحْتِرَازًا عَنِ الرّبوا وَلَابُدَّ مِنَ التَّقَابُضِ فِيْمَا يُقَابِلُ نَصِيبَهِ مِنَ الذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ لِأَنَّهُ صَرْفٌ فِي هَذَا الْقَدْرِ وَلَوْ كَانَ بَدَلُ الصُّلْحِ عَرْضًا جَازَ مُطْلَقًا لِعَدَمِ الرِّبوا وَلَوْ كَانَ فِي التَّرْكَةِ الدَّرَاهِمُ وَالدَّنَانِيرُ وَبَدُلُ الصُّلْحِ دَرَاهِمُ وَدَنَانِيرُ جَازَ الصُّلْحُ كَيْفَ مَا كَانَ صَرْفًا لِلْجِنْسِ إِلَى خِلَافِ الْجِنْسِ كَمَا فِي البَيْعِ لَكِنَّ يُشْتَرَطُ الْتَقَابُضُ لِلصَّرْفِ
ترجمہ اور اگر ترکہ میں سونا چاندی اور اسباب دونوں ہوں اور در شہ وارث مذکورکوصرف سونا یا چاندی دے کر خارج کریں تو یہ تخارج صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ جب تک کہ وہ چاندی یا سونا جو وارث کو دیا ہے اس مقدار سے زیادہ نہ ہو جو وارث کو اسی جنس کے حصے سے پہنچنے والا ہے۔ مثلاً وارث مذکور کو میراث سے دس درہم اور کچھ اسباب پہنچتا ہے تو صحت تخارج کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ دس درہم سے زائد پر صلح ہو۔ تا کہ دس در ہم اس کے عوض میں ہو جائیں اور زائد در ہم اسباب کا عوض ہو جائیں ورنہ سود لازم آئے گا خواہ عوض اس کے حصہ سے کم ہو یا اس کے برابر ہو۔ کیونکہ دونوں صورتوں میں وہ مال جو اسی جنس اور غیر جنس سے ماخوذہ مقدار پر زائد ہے وہ عوض سے خالی رہ جاتا ہے۔ پس دونوں صورتوں میں معاوضہ کے طور پر جائز کرنا محعذر ہے کیونکہ بیاج لازم آتا ہے۔
سوال یہ کیا ضروری ہے کہ تجویز بطریق معاوضہ ہی ہو۔ یہ بھی تو ہو سکتا ہے کہ بطریق ابراء ہو۔ گویا اس نے باقی سے بری کر دیا۔ جواب بطریق ابراء جائز قرار نہیں دے سکتے۔ اس لئے کہ ترکہ مال عین ہے اور اعیان سے بری کرنا باطل ہے۔ کیونکہ اسقاط کا عمل دیون میں ہوتا ہے نہ کہ اعیان میں ، ذخیرہ اور شرح ہدایہ میں ایساہی مذکور ہے۔ لیکن اس پر صاحب نتائج نے کہا ہے کہ بطریق ابراء تجویز کا صحیح نہ ہونا میرے نزدیک محل نظر ہے اس لئے کہ نفس اعیان سے ابراء اگر چہ باطل ہے لیکن دعوی اعیان سے بری کرنا تو حسب تصریح فقہا صحیح ہے اور یہ کتاب میں بھی گزر چکا اور جب عاقل بالغ کے کلام کوحتی الامکان صحیح کرنا ضروری ہے تو طریق ابراء ہی کو اختیار کرنا چاہیے۔
ممکن ہے کوئی یہ کہے کہ کتاب میں یہ مسئلہ گزر چکا کہ اگر کسی نے مکان کا دعوی کیا اور اس کے ایک قطعہ پر صلح ہوگئی تو یہ صلح صحیح نہیں ۔ کیونکہ جو کچھ مدعی نے لیا ہے وہ اس کا عین حق ہے اور باقی میں وہ اپنے دھونے پر ہے اور زیر بحث مسئلہ بالکل اس مسئلہ کی نظیر ہے۔ پس جب اس مسئلہ میں صلح صحیح نہیں ہوئی تو اس مسئلہ میں کیسے صحیح ہو سکتی ہے۔؟ جواب یہ ہے کہ جہاں وہ مسئلہ گزرا ہے وہیں ارباب شروح نے اس کی تصریح بھی کی ہے۔ کہ یہ غیر ظاہر الروایہ کا جواب ہے ظاہر الروایہ یہی ہے ر صلح صحیح ہے۔ قـولـه ولا بد من التقابض .. الخ - پھر مذکورہ صورت میں اس کے سونے چاندی والے حصہ کے مقابلہ میں جتنا عوض نقد ہے اس پر اسی مجلس میں قبضہ ہو جانا ضروری ہے کیونکہ اس مقدار میں مسلہ بھی بیچ صرف ہے اور بچے صرف میں تقابض نی انجلس شرط ہے اور اگر بدل صلح کوئی اسباب ہو تو صلح مطلقاً جائز ہے۔ قبضہ ہو یا نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ اب کسی صورت میں بیان متحقق نہ ہوگا۔
And if the estate is gold and silver and other than that, and they make a sulh with him on silver or gold, then it is necessary that what they give him is more than his share of that genus, so that his share is equivalent to it, and the excess is for his right from the remainder of the estate, to avoid riba. And hand-to-hand possession is necessary in what corresponds to his share of gold and silver because it is ṣarf in this amount. And if the consideration of sulh is goods, it is absolutely permissible due to the absence of riba. And if in the estate there are dirhams and dinars, and the consideration of sulh is dirhams and dinars, the sulh is permissible in whatever manner, turning the genus to a different genus as in sale, but hand-to-hand possession is required due to ṣarf. Translation: And if the estate contains gold, silver, and goods, and the mentioned heir is taken out (ikhraj) by giving him only gold or silver, then this takhāruj will not be valid unless the silver or gold given to him is more than the amount that would reach him from his share of that genus. For example, if the mentioned heir gets ten dirhams and some goods from the inheritance, then for the validity of takhāruj it is necessary that the sulh be for more than ten dirhams, so that the ten dirhams become in exchange for his share of silver, and the excess dirhams become in exchange for the goods; otherwise riba will become necessary, whether the consideration is less than his share or equal. Because in both cases, the property that is of the same genus and taken more than the amount of that genus becomes free of consideration. So in both cases, making it permissible as a mu'āwaḍah is difficult because riba becomes necessary. Question: Is it necessary that the arrangement be by way of mu'āwaḍah? It could also be by way of ibrā' (release); as if he has been released from the remainder. Answer: It cannot be deemed permissible by way of ibrā' because the estate is ʿayn (tangible property), and ibrā' from ʿayn is invalid, since dropping (isqāṭ) applies to debts, not to ʿayn. Such is mentioned in Dhakhīrah and Sharḥ al-Hidāyah. However, the author of Natā'ij said: that the arrangement by ibrā' not being valid is, in my view, open to consideration, because ibrā' from the very ʿayn is invalid, but ibrā' from the claim of ʿayn is valid according to the explicit statements of jurists, and this has also passed in the book. And when it is necessary to interpret the speech of a sane adult as correctly as possible, the method of ibrā' should be adopted. It is possible that one may say: This issue has passed in the book that if someone claimed a house and a sulh was made on one piece of it, that sulh is not valid because what the claimant took is his exact right, and regarding the remainder he persists in his claim, and the issue under discussion is exactly analogous to that issue. So when sulh was not valid in that issue, how can it be valid in this issue? The answer is that where that issue passed, the commentators have specified that it is a response from non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah; the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is that the sulh is valid. His statement: 'and hand-to-hand possession is necessary' etc. Then in the mentioned scenario, in exchange for his share of gold and silver, whatever cash consideration there is, possession in the same session is necessary because in that amount the transaction is also a ṣarf sale, and in ṣarf, possession in the session is a condition. And if the consideration of sulh is goods, the sulh is absolutely permissible, whether possession occurs or not, because now no form of riba will be realized.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with critical refinement. It addresses sulh when the estate contains both gold/silver and other goods, and the settlement is only in gold or silver. To avoid riba, the amount given must exceed the heir's share of that specific genus; the excess then compensates for the heir's share of the other goods. If the amount equals or is less, riba occurs because the heir's share of gold/silver is not fully compensated. The commentary then engages in a dispute: can the arrangement be considered as ibrā' (release) instead of mu'āwaḍah? The initial view says no, because ibrā' from ʿayn (tangible property) is invalid. However, a later authority, Ṣāḥib al-Natā'ij, objects, arguing that ibrā' from a claim to ʿayn is valid, and since the heir's speech should be interpreted correctly, it can be considered ibrā'. This is a critical refinement. Then a question arises from a previous case about a house: why is sulh on part of a claimed house invalid, but here sulh on part of the estate is valid? The answer is that the previous case was from non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah; the relied-upon position (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah) is that it is valid. Finally, the condition of taqābuḍ is reiterated: for the portion of the settlement that corresponds to the heir's share of gold/silver, hand-to-hand possession in the session is required because it is ṣarf. If the settlement consists of goods, no such condition is needed as there is no riba.

Key Terms
ابراء (ibrā'): Release or discharge from a claim; in this context, whether the heir can be considered to have released his right to the remaining estate in return for the gold/silver received.
تخارج (takhāruj): A form of sulh where one heir takes some property and exits the estate, leaving the rest to the others.
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The authoritative transmitted rulings from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani; the relied-upon position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 10 dirhams
B) More than 10 dirhams
C) Any amount
D) The value of his entire share in goods

Key Takeaway
In sulh with mixed estate, giving more than the heir's share of the same genus is essential to avoid riba; a later view allows it as ibrā' from claim, easing strictness.

Definition of ʿĀriyah and Ownership of Usufruct
Defends the definition of ʿāriyah as tamlīk of manāfiʿ via qiyas and responds to objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ʿāriyah as tamlīk of manāfiʿ and apply the qiyas argument to defend the ownership of usufruct against the objection that they are non-enduring accidents.

Core Idea
Usufruct can be owned gratuitously because the need that justifies ownership of physical objects also applies to usufruct.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidāyah addresses a foundational question: Can usufruct (the benefits of a thing) be owned without compensation? The Hanafi school answers yes, and here the author defends that position against Imām Karkhī and others, using a qiyas argument grounded in the common cause of fulfilling need. You will explore the definition, the proof, and the methodological objections that refine the argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept being defined
The passage defines ʿāriyah as tamlīk (transfer of ownership) of manāfiʿ (usufruct) without compensation. Note its derivation from ʿaryah (gift).
This contrasts with views that treat ʿāriyah as mere permission (ibāḥah).
2
Analyze the objection to usufruct ownership
An opponent argues that usufruct are accidents (aʿrāḍ) that do not endure, so they cannot be owned. Understand the basis of this objection.
3
Examine the Hanafi response via qiyas
The text uses qiyas: physical objects (aʿyān) can be owned with or without compensation (sale/gift). The common cause (ʿillah) is fulfilling a need (dafʿ al-hājah), which also applies to usufruct, so usufruct can be owned in both ways (lease/loan).
The qiyas is jaliy (clear analogy) because the ʿillah is evident.
4
Understand the three methodological objections and replies
Al-ʿInāyah raises objections: 1) istidlāl in definitions, 2) qiyas on non-legal subjects, 3) lack of complete similarity. Each is refuted by clarifying the object of inference and the nature of qiyas.
Focus on the distinction between definition and implicit ruling, and the sufficiency of shared ʿillah.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi position
The Hanafi position stands: ʿāriyah is a valid contract of tamlīk of usufruct, supported by qiyas and the principle from al-Zaylaʿī that anything permitting tamlīk with a consideration also permits it without, except marriage.

A person who owns something without compensation can make another owner of it with compensation, like the recipient of a gift. He said: And we say... In response to Imām Karkhī, we say that the word 'āriyah conveys the meaning of tamlīk because it is derived from 'aryah meaning gift. Therefore, 'āriyah is concluded with the word tamlīk, as when one says: 'I grant you ownership of the usufruct of this house for a month' (mentioned in al-Mabsūṭ). It is possible that someone might say: usufruct are accidents which do not endure, so they are not capable of being owned. The author of al-Hidāyah, through his statement 'and usufruct are capable of ownership like physical objects', replies that usufruct are also capable of ownership like physical objects, because tamlīk is of two types: one with compensation and the second without compensation. Then physical objects are capable of both types (tamlīk of a physical object with compensation like sale, and without compensation like gift), so usufruct will also be capable of both types (tamlīk of usufruct with compensation like lease, and tamlīk of usufruct without compensation like 'āriyah), because the comprehensive factor, i.e., fulfilling a need, exists in both. Al-Zaylaʿī said: Everything in which tamlīk with a consideration is valid, tamlīk without consideration is also valid, except marriage. Note: The author of al-ʿInāyah raised three objections here. First objection: The statement of the author of al-Hidāyah is an istidlāl within definitions, while definitions do not accept istidlāl because definitions are from the category of concepts (taṣawwurāt) and istidlāl occurs in affirmations (taṣdīqāt). The response: Here the istidlāl is not on the definition itself, but on the implicit ruling that the definer intends, such as saying 'this definition is correct, this definition is true, this definition is correct, comprehensive, and exclusive' etc. As is clear in its place, the objections of preventiveness, deficiency, and opposition that are raised against definitions are on these implicit rulings, not on the definitions themselves. Second objection: The mentioned qiyās (that usufruct are capable of ownership like physical objects) is about matter-of-fact things, which is not valid because qiyās requires that a legal ruling established by textual evidence be transferred to the branch that is its counterpart, and here there is no textual evidence. Also, matter-of-fact things are not legal rulings. The response: The author of al-Hidāyah does not intend to prove by qiyās that the word 'āriyah is designated in the Sharīʿah for tamlīk of usufruct without compensation, such that the objection of qiyās on matter-of-fact things would apply. Rather, he intends to prove through qiyās to physical objects, which are capable of both types of tamlīk, that usufruct are also capable of both types. With this proof, he only intends to remove the objector's illusion that accidents, because they do not endure, cannot be owned. And it is obvious that physical objects' acceptance of both types of tamlīk is a legal ruling established by textual evidence, which is indicated by the verses on sale and gift. So it is valid to transfer it to the acceptance of usufruct for both types as well. Third objection: Qiyās also requires that the legal ruling be transferred to the branch that is its counterpart, and here usufruct are not the counterpart of physical objects. The response: If 'not counterpart' means that they are not similar in all respects, then that is conceded, but it does not benefit the objector because qiyās does not require complete similarity in all aspects; it is sufficient that they share the cause (ʿillah) of the ruling, as known from uṣūl al-fiqh. If 'not counterpart' means that they are not similar even in the cause of the ruling, then that is not conceded because here tamlīk is the ruling, and its cause is fulfilling a need, and both physical objects and usufruct share this cause. (Results)
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on al-Hidāyah, addressing the definition of ʿāriyah (gratuitous loan) and the capacity of usufruct (manāfiʿ) for ownership. The author begins by stating that one who owns an object without compensation can make another owner of it with compensation, like a gift recipient. Then he responds to Imām Karkhī by arguing that the word ʿāriyah implies tamlīk (transfer of ownership) because it derives from ʿaryah meaning gift. Thus, ʿāriyah is concluded with the word tamlīk, as in 'I grant you ownership of the usufruct of this house for a month' (cited from al-Mabsūṭ). An objector claims that usufruct are accidents (aʿrāḍ) that do not endure, so they cannot be owned. The author of al-Hidāyah replies that usufruct are capable of ownership like physical objects (aʿyān), because tamlīk has two forms: with compensation and without compensation. Physical objects can be owned in both ways (sale and gift), so usufruct can also be owned in both ways (lease and loan). The common cause (ʿillah) is fulfilling a need (dafʿ al-hājah). Al-Zaylaʿī supports with the principle that whatever permits tamlīk with consideration also permits tamlīk without consideration, except marriage. Then follows a note (tanbīh) with three objections from the author of al-ʿInāyah and their responses. The first objection is that using istidlāl (inference) in definitions is invalid because definitions are concepts (taṣawwurāt) not affirmations (taṣdīqāt). The response is that the inference is not on the definition itself but on the implicit claim that the definition is correct, which is an affirmation. The second objection is that the qiyās is on the subject (mawḍūʿāt) of the term, which is not a legal ruling. The response is that the qiyās is not to prove the linguistic designation but to prove that usufruct are capable of ownership, based on the legal ruling for physical objects established by textual evidence. The third objection is that usufruct are not counterparts of physical objects for qiyās. The response is that complete similarity is not required only sharing the cause (ʿillah). Here, the cause is fulfilling a need, common to both. This establishes the Hanafi position that usufruct can be owned gratuitously, making ʿāriyah a valid contract of tamlīk.

Key Terms
عاریت (ʿāriyah): Gratuitous loan; transfer of ownership of usufruct without compensation, revocable at will
منافع (manāfiʿ): Usufruct; the benefits derived from property, considered as aʿrāḍ (accidents) in Hanafī thought
تملیک (tamlīk): Transfer of ownership; making someone the owner of something

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī position in this passage, why are usufruct (manāfiʿ) considered capable of ownership (qābilah li al-milk)?
A) Because they are physical objects like aʿyān
B) Because the need (dafʿ al-hājah) that justifies tamlīk of aʿyān also applies to manāfiʿ
C) Because the word ʿāriyah derives from ʿaryah meaning gift
D) Because al-Zaylaʿī said so

Key Takeaway
ʿĀriyah is a valid contract of tamlīk of usufruct because the same need that justifies ownership of physical objects also justifies ownership of benefits.

The Use of Ibāḥah for Tamlīk in ʿĀriyah
Ruling with proof: defends the validity of ibāḥah for ʿāriyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using the word ibāḥah for ʿāriyah, explain the analogy with ijārah, and apply the reasoning to reject objections about jahālah and prohibition.

Core Idea
Ibāḥah in ʿāriyah is a valid metaphor for tamlīk, as the non-binding nature makes ignorance harmless and possession removes uncertainty.

This passage addresses a key Hanafi principle: the word ibāḥah (permission) can be used to create a contract of ʿāriyah (gratuitous loan) because it is metaphorically taken to mean tamlīk (transfer of ownership of usufruct). The author uses an analogy with ijārah (lease), which is also concluded by the word ibāḥah, and responds to four objections raised by Imām Karkhī. Understanding this reasoning clarifies why jahālah (ignorance) of duration does not invalidate the contract, and how the lender's explicit prohibition can nullify the permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
State that the word ibāḥah is validly used to conclude a contract of ʿāriyah because it is metaphorically borrowed for tamlīk.
This is the central ruling being defended.
2
Locate the proof (dalīl)
The proof is qiyās (analogy) with ijārah: since ijārah is valid with the word ibāḥah, even though it involves tamlīk of usufruct, ʿāriyah follows the same rule.
The analogy relies on the shared illa (effective cause) of transferring usufruct.
3
Analyze the response to the jahālah objection
Explain that ignorance of duration does not cause dispute because ʿāriyah is ghayr lāzim (non-binding); the lender can take back the object at any time, so duration is irrelevant.
This distinguishes ʿāriyah from binding contracts like sale.
4
Examine the possession (qabḍ) argument
Ownership in ʿāriyah is established only upon possession (qabḍ), which is the actual taking of benefit. At that point there is no ignorance about the duration because the benefit is received instantly.
The object's return is not tied to a specific time frame.
5
Understand the effect of prohibition (nahy)
If the lender explicitly forbids the borrower from taking benefit, then the permission is void; the usufruct does not come into the borrower's ownership because the contract only transfers ownership when accompanied by implied permission.
This clarifies that nahy nullifies the tamlīk effect of ibāḥah.

وَلَفْظَةُ الْإِبَاحَةِ أَسْتَعِيرَتْ لِلتَّمْلِيْكِ كَمَا فِي الْإِجَارَةِ فَإِنَّهَا تَنْعَقِدُ بِلَفْظِةِ الْإِبَاحَةِ وَهِيَ تَمْلِيْكَ وَالْجَهَالَةُ لَا تُفْضِي إِلَى الْمُنَازَعَةِ لِعَدْمِ اللُّزُومِ فَلَا تَكُونُ صَائِرَةً وَ لاَ الْمِلْكَ إِنَّمَا يَثْبُتُ بِالْقَبْضِ وَهُوَ ا لْانْتِفَاعُ وَعِنْدَ ذلِكَ لَا جِهَالَةَ وَالنَّهَى مَنع عَنِ التَّحْصِيلِ فَلَا يَتَحَصَّلَ الْمُنَافِعُ عَلَى مِلْكِهِ وَلَا يَمْلِكُ الْإِجَارَةَ لِدَفْعِ زِيَادَةِ الضَّرَرِ عَلَى مَا نَذْكُرُهُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى
