جواب یہ ہے کہ منع مغیر کا مؤثر ہونا اس اعتبار سے نہیں ہے کہ عاریت میں تملیک نہیں ہوتی بلکہ اس اعتبار سے ہے کہ معیر نے مال مستعار نفع لینے کی ممانعت کردی۔ تو اب منافع اس کی ملک پر حاصل نہ ہوں گے۔
Ruling of ʿĀriyah with the Word Ibāḥah
And the word ibāḥah is borrowed metaphorically for tamlīk, just as in lease (ijārah), for it is concluded with the word ibāḥah, and it is tamlīk. And ignorance (jahālah) does not lead to dispute due to the absence of bindingness, so it is not harmful. And because ownership is only established by possession (qabḍ), and possession is the taking of benefit, and at that time there is no ignorance. And prohibition (al-nahy) is a prevention from acquisition, so the usufruct does not come into his ownership, and he does not own the lease to repel additional harm, as we will mention, if Allah wills.
Translation: And the word ibāḥah is borrowed for tamlīk, as in lease, for it is concluded with the word ibāḥah while it is tamlīk. And ignorance does not lead to dispute due to the absence of bindingness, so it is not harmful. And because ownership is only established by possession, and possession is the taking of benefit, and at that time there is no ignorance. Otherwise, there is a prohibition from acquiring benefit. So usufruct will not come into his ownership, and he does not own the lease to repel additional harm, as we will mention, if Allah wills.
Explanation: His statement 'and the word ibāḥah...' is a response to the four reasons of Imām Karkhī. The response is that the validity of using ibāḥah is because the word ibāḥah is taken metaphorically in the sense of tamlīk, just as lease is concluded with the word ibāḥah, even though it means tamlīk of usufruct, about which there is no dispute. The response is that here there is no such ignorance that leads to dispute because ʿāriyah is not a binding contract; the lender can rescind whenever he wishes, so ignorance of the duration is not harmful. Moreover, in ʿāriyah, ownership is only established when possession takes place, and possession in ʿāriyah means to derive benefit, and at the time of benefit there is no ignorance. The response is that the effect of the lender's prohibition is not that ʿāriyah does not involve tamlīk, but rather that the lender has prevented the borrower from taking benefit. So the usufruct will not come into his ownership.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining that the word ibāḥah (permission) can be used to conclude a contract of ʿāriyah because it is metaphorically used for tamlīk (transfer of ownership). The author draws an analogy with lease (ijārah), which is also concluded with the word ibāḥah. Four possible objections (from Imām Karkhī) are addressed. First, that ibāḥah does not imply tamlīk; the response is that it does by metaphor, just like in lease. Second, that ignorance of the duration (jahālah al-muddah) would cause dispute; the response is that since ʿāriyah is non-binding (ghayr lāzim), any ignorance does not lead to conflict because the lender may revoke at any time. Third, that ownership is not established until possession (qabḍ), and possession is the actual taking of benefit, at which point there is no ignorance about the duration. Fourth, that the lender's prohibition (nahy) prevents the acquisition of ownership; the response distinguishes between the contract and the actual permission: if the lender explicitly prohibits taking benefit, then the borrower does not own the usufruct, because the contract only transfers ownership when accompanied by the implied permission. This clarifies that ʿāriyah is valid with the word ibāḥah, relying on the Hanafi principle that the word ibāḥah can effectively transfer ownership of usufruct because of the need and custom.

Key Terms
اباحہ (ibāḥah): Permission; in this context, it is a word used metaphorically for tamlīk in ʿāriyah and ijārah
جہالت (jahālah): Ignorance of a term or condition, such as the duration of the loan
لزوم (luzūm): Bindingness; the quality of a contract that prevents unilateral rescission

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī position in this passage, why does the ignorance of duration (jahālah al-muddah) not invalidate ʿāriyah?
A) Because the lender must specify the exact duration
B) Because ʿāriyah is a binding contract (lāzim), so ignorance does not matter
C) Because ʿāriyah is non-binding (ghayr lāzim); the lender may revoke at any time, so ignorance does not lead to dispute
D) Because the borrower can always return the item, so duration is irrelevant

Key Takeaway
The word ibāḥah validly transfers ownership of usufruct in ʿāriyah because it is metaphorical, the contract is non-binding, possession removes uncertainty, and only explicit prohibition nullifies the permission.

Ruling: The Borrower Cannot Sub-Lease the Borrowed Item
States that the borrower cannot lease the item to another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sub-leasing in aariyah and explain why the prohibition exists based on the lender's right to revoke.

Core Idea
The borrower cannot sub-lease because the lender's right to revoke would be blocked by a binding lease.

In the Hanafi school, a contract of aariyah (loan for use) gives the borrower only temporary possession, not full ownership of the usufruct. The lender retains the right to revoke the loan at any time. This lesson examines why the borrower cannot sub-lease the borrowed item to a third party, based on a passage from a commentary on Al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key actors
Understand the roles: musta'ir (borrower), mu'ir (lender), and the third party lessee.
The borrower is a trustee (amin), not an owner.
2
State the ruling
The musta'ir cannot give the borrowed item on ijarah (lease) to another person.
This ruling is makruh tahrimi (prohibited) without the mu'ir's permission.
3
Analyze the rationale
The mu'ir owns the usufruct and can revoke the loan anytime. An ijarah contract is binding (lazim), which would block revocation and cause harm.
The maxim: 'No harm and no reciprocating harm' (la darar wa la dirar).
4
Contrast with ijarah
Ijarah is binding in Hanafi fiqh; aariyah is non-binding for the lender. This distinction is crucial.
If the borrower leased the item, the mu'ir could not reclaim it until the lease ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۴۔ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مستعیر دوسرے شخص کو اجارہ پر اس لئے نہیں دے سکتا تا کہ اس سے معیر پر زیادہ ضر لاحق نہ ہو اسلئے کہ معیر ۔ منافع کا مالک اس طور پر بنایا ہے کہ جب چاہے گا واپس لے گا اور اجارہ پر دینے کی صورت میں معیر واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ عقد اجارہ شرعاً لازمی ہوتا ہے۔
The answer to [question] 4 is that the borrower cannot give [the item] to another person on lease, so that it does not cause greater harm to the lender, because the lender owns the usufruct in such a way that whenever he wishes he will take it back, and in the case of giving on lease, the lender cannot take it back, because the contract of lease is binding (lazim) by sharia.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the limits of aariyah (loan). The musta'ir (borrower) is not permitted to sub-lease the borrowed item to a third party. The reasoning is that the mu'ir (lender) retains ownership of the usufruct (manafi') and has the right to revoke the loan at any time. If the borrower leases the item, the lease contract would be binding (lazim) and the mu'ir could not reclaim the item during the lease term, thereby causing harm. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that aariyah is a non-binding contract (ghayr lazim) for the mu'ir, while ijara is binding. The passage is from a commentary on Al-Hidayah, possibly addressing an objection.

Key Terms
مستعیر (musta'ir): The borrower in a contract of aariyah (loan of a tangible item for use).
معیر (mu'ir): The lender in a contract of aariyah.
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract of hire or lease for a known rent and period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can the musta'ir (borrower) lease the borrowed item to a third person without the mu'ir's permission?
A) Yes, because he has possession of the item.
B) No, because it would harm the mu'ir who can revoke at any time.
C) Yes, if the term is short.
D) No, because the item is also owned by the musta'ir.

Key Takeaway
The borrower cannot sub-lease without permission because the lender's right to revoke must remain unimpeded.

Valid Wordings for Aariyah Contract
Lists and classifies valid aariyah wordings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify valid Arabic wordings for aariyah and classify each as sarih haqiqah (explicit literal), sarih majaz (explicit metaphorical), or ambiguous, applying the Hanafi principle of haml (carrying to usufruct) when ownership transfer is not intended.

Core Idea
Many wordings create a valid aariyah, but only 'a'aratuka' is literal; others are metaphorical or require the absence of hibah intention.

In Hanafi fiqh, a contract of aariyah (loan of an item for its usufruct) can be formed through various Arabic phrases. This lesson from Al-Hidayah lists the valid wordings and distinguishes between those that are explicitly literal, those that are common metaphors, and those that become valid only when the context rules out transfer of ownership. Understanding these nuances prevents disputes over whether the transaction was a gift or a loan.

Guided Path
1
List the wordings from the text
Read the source passage and extract all the Arabic phrases mentioned as valid for aariyah: 'a'aratuka', 'at'amtu-ka hadhihi al-ard', 'manah'tuka thawbi', 'hamaltuka 'ala dabbati', 'akhdamtuka hadha al-'abd', 'dari laka sukna', and 'dari laka 'umra sukna'.
The text also adds a hadith about revocability but our focus is on wordings.
2
Classify each wording by clarity
Determine which wordings are sarih haqiqah (explicit literal: 'a'aratuka'), sarih majaz (explicit metaphorical: 'at'amtu' is majaz muta'arif), and which are ambiguous and require the absence of hibah intention ('manah'tuka' and 'hamaltuka' because they are literal for tamlik al-ayn but are carried to tamlik al-manafi' figuratively when hibah is not intended).
'At'amtu' is metaphorical because it adds 'land' (non-eatable), while 'manah'tu' and 'hamaltu' are literal for ownership transfer but are reinterpreted.
3
Apply the principle of haml (carrying)
For 'manah'tuka' and 'hamaltuka', the default literal meaning is tamlik al-ayn (transfer of ownership). However, when the speaker does not intend hibah, the word is carried (yuhmalu) to tamlik al-manafi' (transfer of usufruct) by isti'mal majazi (figurative usage) because aariyah is more cautious (muhtamin).
The commentary explains that this is only when hibah is not intended; otherwise it could be a gift.
4
Interpret remaining wordings
'Akhdamtuka' is an explicit permission for service. 'Dari laka sukna' uses 'sukna' to clarify that the transfer is of dwelling, not ownership. 'Dari laka 'umra sukna' specifies a life grant of dwelling. In both 'laka' is ambiguous between ownership and usufruct, but the word 'sukna' interprets it as usufruct.
This shows how additional context (like 'sukna') can resolve ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَتَصِحُ بِقَوْلِهِ آعَرْتُكَ لأَنَّهُ صَرِيحٌ فِيهِ وَأَطْعَمْتُكَ هَذِهِ الْأَرْضَ لِأَنَّهُ مُسْتَعْمَلْ فِيهِ وَمَنَحْتُكَ لِهَذَا القَوْبَ وَحَمَلْتُكَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الدَّابَّةِ إِذَا لَمْ يُرِدْ بِهِ الْهِبَةَ لِأَنَّهُمَا لِتَمْلِيكِ الْعَيْنِ وَعِنْدَ عَدْمٍ إِرَادَتِهِ الْهِبَةِ يُحْمَلُ عَلَى تَمْلِيكَ الْمَنَافِعِ تَجَوُّزًا. قَالَ وَاَحْدَمْتُكَ هذَا الْعَبْدَ لِاَنَّهُ إِذْنٌ لَهُ فِي إِسْتِخْدَامِهِ وَدَارِي لَكَ سُكْنَى لِأَنَّ مَعْنَاهُ سُكْنَاهَا لَكَ وَدَارِى لَكَ عُمْراى سُكْنى لِأَنَّهُ جَعَلَ سُكْنَاهَا لَهُ مُدَّةَ عُمُرِهِ وَجَعَلَ قَوْلِهِ سُكْنَى تَفْسِيرًا لِقَوْلِهِ لَكَ لِأَنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ تَمْلِيْكَ الْمَنَافِعِ فَجُمَل عَلَيْهِ بِدَلَالَةِ آخِرِهِ.
ترجمہ: اور عاریت صحیح ہے یہ کہنے سے میں نے تجھے مانگی دی۔ کیونکہ یہ لفظ اس میں صریح ہے اور کھانے کے لئے یہ زمین دی۔ کیونکہ یہ لفظ اسی معنی میں مستعمل ہے اور بخش دیا تجھ کو یہ کپڑا۔ اور وار کیا تجھ کو اس جانور پر جب کہ ان دونوں سے ہبہ مراد نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں لفظ تملیک عین کے لئے ہیں۔ اور ہبہ مراد نہ ہونے کے وقت مجاز اتملیک منافع پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ اور خدمت کے لئے دے دیا۔ تجھ کو یہ غلام کیونکہ یہ غلام سے خدمت لینے کی اجازت ہے۔ اور میرا گھر تیرے رہنے کے لئے ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اس گھر کی سکونت تیرے لئے ہے۔ اور میرا گھر تیرے عمر بھر رہنے کے لئے ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اس گھر کی رہائش اس کے لئے اس کی مدت عمر تک کر دی اور لفظ سکنی کو اپنے قول لک کی تفسیر کر دیا اس لئے کہ یہ تملیک منافع کو بھی متحمل ہے تو اس کے آخر کی دلالت سے اس پر محمول کیا گیا اور مغیر کو اختیار ہے کہ واپس لے لے عاریت جب چاہے کیونکہ حضور علیہ اسلام کا ارشاد ہے کہ دی ہوئی چیز واپس کی جائے گی اور مانگی چیز واپس پہنچائی جائے گی ۔ اور اس لئے کہ منافع تھوڑے تھوڑے ملک میں آئے ہیں۔ ان کے پیدا ہونے کے حساب سے پس جو بھی نہیں پائے گئے ان سے قبضہ متصل نہیں ہوا لہذا ان سے رجوع کرنا صحیح ہے۔
تشریح: قوله و تصح بقوله اعرتك ..... عاریت مذکورہ ذیل الفاظ سے صحیح ہو جاتی ہے۔ اعر تك کیونکہ یہ لفظ عاریت کیلئے صریح اور حقیقت ہے۔ اطعمتک ارضی کیونکہ یہ الفاظ اسی معنی میں مستعمل ہیں اس لئے کہ جب الفاظ اطعام کی اضافت غیر ماکول العین کی طرف ہو تو اس سے مجاز أحال پر محل کا اطلاق کرتے ہوئے اس کی پیداوار مراد ہوتی ہے۔ سوال .... یہ استعمال مجاز متعارف ہوا اور مجاز متعارف بھی صریح ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ اصول میں مذکور ہے۔ پس دونوں عبارتوں میں کوئی فرق نہ ہوا۔ ....... جواب ... مذکورہ دونوں لفظ صریح ہیں مگر ایک حقیقت ہے اور دوسرا مجاز ہے اس لئے کہ علماء اصول کے یہاں صریح وہ ہے جس کی مراد فی نفسہ واضح ہو۔ پس یہ حقیقت غیر مہجورہ اور مجاز متعارف دونوں کو شامل ہیں۔ پس صاحب ہدایہ نے مستعمل بول کر اشارہ کر دیا کہ پہلا لفظ حقیقت ہے۔ اور دوسرا مجاز ۔ قوله منحتك منحتك ثوبي حملتك على دابتی سے بھی عاریت صحیح ہوگی۔ کیونکہ مختک کے معنیٰ ہیں۔ اعطيتك يـقـال نحر (فض) مخالشئی بمعنی دینا عطاء کرنا۔ اس دودھ والی بکری یا اونٹنی کو کہتے ہیں جو کسی کو دودھ پینے کے لئے دے دی جائے اور جب دودھ ختم ہو جائے تو مالک کو واپس کر دے۔ پھر ہر عطاء میں اس کا استعمال کثیر ہو گیا۔ اس طرح اور اس سے مراد تملیک ہوتی ہے۔ پس منحت اور حملت میں سے ہر ایک تملیک منفعت اور تملیک عین کے لئے حقیقت ہے ۔ تو نیت نہ ہو کے وقت عاریت پر محمول ہوں گے کہ وہ متقین ہے (مگر یہ اس وقت ہے جب ان سے ہبہ کی نیت نہ کی ہو ) ۔
He said: And [aariyah] is valid by his saying 'I lend you' because it is explicit in it, and 'I fed you this land' because it is used in it, and 'I granted you this cloth' and 'I mounted you on this animal' when he does not intend hibah by them, because both are for tamlik al-ayn (transfer of ownership of the substance), and when hibah is not intended, it is carried upon tamlik al-manafi' (transfer of usufruct) figuratively. He said: And 'I gave you this slave for service' because it is permission for him to use him, and 'my house is for you to dwell in' because its meaning is dwelling in it for you, and 'my house is for you as a life grant of dwelling' because he made its dwelling for him for the duration of his life, and he made his saying 'sukna' an interpretation of his saying 'laka' because it may bear tamlik al-manafi', so it is carried upon that by the indication of its end. Translation: And aariyah is valid by his saying 'I lent you' because this word is explicit for it, and 'I fed you this land' because this word is used in this meaning, and 'I granted you this cloth' and 'I mounted you on this animal' when he does not intend hibah by them, because both words are for tamlik al-ayn, and when hibah is not intended, they are carried upon tamlik al-manafi' figuratively. And 'I gave you this slave for service' because it is permission to take service from him. And 'my house is for you to dwell in' because its meaning is dwelling in it for you. And 'my house is for you as a life grant of dwelling' because he made its dwelling for him for the duration of his life, and he made the word sukna an interpretation of his word laka because it may bear tamlik al-manafi', so it is carried upon that by the indication of its end. And the lender has the right to take back the loan whenever he wishes because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The gift is returned and the loan is repaid.' And because usufruct comes into ownership little by little according to their occurrence; what has not yet come into existence, possession has not been connected to it, so revoking it is valid. Commentary: His saying 'and it is valid by his saying I lend you'... Aariyah becomes valid by the following words: 'a'artuka' because this word is explicit and literal for aariyah. 'at'amtu-ka ardi' because these words are used in this meaning, because when the word it'am is added to a non-eatable substance, it is a metaphor for giving its produce. Question: This usage is a common metaphor (majaz muta'arif) and common metaphor is also explicit (sarih) as mentioned in usul. So there is no difference between the two expressions. Answer: Both words are explicit, but one is literal (haqiqah) and the other is metaphorical (majaz), because according to usul scholars, sarih is that whose intended meaning is clear in itself. So it includes both non-abandoned literal and common metaphorical. So the author of Hidayah said 'musta'mal' (used) to indicate that the first word is literal and the second is metaphorical. His saying 'manah'tuka': aariyah is also valid by 'manah'tuka thawbi' and 'hamaltuka 'ala dabbati'. Because the meaning of 'manah'tu' is 'a'taytuka' (I gave you). It is said 'nahara (fadd) makhluq' meaning giving. It is a she-goat or she-camel given for milking, to be returned when milk stops. Then its usage became frequent for every gift. And it is intended for tamlik (transfer of ownership). So both 'manah'tu' and 'hamaltu' are literal for tamlik al-manafi' and tamlik al-'ayn. So when there is no intention, they are carried upon aariyah because it is more cautious (but this is when hibah is not intended).
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage defines the valid wordings (alfaz) for a contract of aariyah (loan of a tangible item for use). It is from Al-Hidayah with a detailed Urdu commentary (Ashraf al-Hidayah). The primary text states that aariyah is valid with clear words like 'a'artuka' (I lend you), and with words like 'at'amtu-ka hadhihi al-ard' (I fed you this land) because it is used in that sense, and with 'manah'tuka' and 'hamaltuka' when hibah is not intended, because these words are primarily for tamlik al-ayn but if hibah is not intended, they are interpreted figuratively for tamlik al-manafi'. The commentary clarifies the distinction between literal (haqiqah) and common metaphorical (majaz muta'arif) usage, and responds to a potential objection that both are explicit. The conclusion is that 'a'artuka' is literal, while 'at'amtu' is metaphorical but still explicit. The passage also covers 'akhdamtuka' (I gave you for service), 'dari laka sukna' (my house is for you to dwell in), and 'umra sukna' (life grant of dwelling). The lender's right to revoke at any time is also reaffirmed with the hadith 'al-minhatu mardudah wa al-ariyatu mu'adah' (the gift is returned and the loan is repaid).

Key Terms
عاریت (aariyah): A contract of loan of a tangible item for its usufruct without compensation.
صریح (sarih): A word that is clear in its meaning without need for interpretation.
تملیک عین (tamlik al-ayn): Transfer of ownership of the substance of the item.
تملیک منافع (tamlik al-manafi'): Transfer of ownership of the usufruct of the item.
مجاز متعارف (majaz muta'arif): A common metaphorical usage that has become well-known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following phrases is considered explicit literal (haqiqah) for aariyah according to the author?
A) at'amtu-ka hadhihi al-ard
B) manah'tuka thawbi
C) a'aratuka
D) hamaltuka 'ala dabbati

Key Takeaway
Valid aariyah wordings range from literal ('a'aratuka') to common metaphor ('at'amtu') to words carried to usufruct when hibah is not intended ('manah'tuka', 'hamaltuka'), all recognized by the Hanafi school.

Linguistic Interpretation of 'Manah'tuka' and 'Hamaltuka' in Hanafi Fiqh
Critical refinement (tanbih) on the interpretation of 'manah'tuka' and 'hamaltuka'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hidayah's original ruling on the interpretation of 'manah'tuka' and 'hamaltuka', identify Allamah Ali's three objections, and explain the resolutions offered by Hanafi authorities.

Core Idea
Words have multiple layers; Hanafi jurists debate whether 'manah'tuka' implies gift or loan of usufruct.

In Hanafi contract law, the precise meaning of words like 'manah'tuka' (I granted you) and 'hamaltuka' (I mounted you) determines whether a transaction is a gift (hibah) or a loan for usufruct (aariyah). The Hidayah ruled that without intention of hibah, these words are carried figuratively upon tamlik al-manafi' (transfer of usufruct). But Allamah Ali in Al-Kafi raised sharp objections. This lesson unpacks the linguistic and legal reasoning behind this dispute, showing how Hanafi scholars refined their positions through multiple probabilities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original claim
Recall what the Hidayah stated: the words 'manah'tuka' and 'hamaltuka' are carried figuratively (majaz) upon tamlik al-manafi' when hibah is not intended.
The Hidayah's default was that these words are literally for tamlik al-ayn (transfer of ownership/hibah) and metaphorically for usufruct.
2
Understand Allamah Ali's three objections
Analyze each objection: (1) the phrasing 'idha lam' should be dual; (2) inconsistency with Al-Bahiyyah where 'hamaltuka' is treated as aariyah but can bear hibah; (3) if words are literal for tamlik al-ayn, they should be carried upon hibah, not usufruct.
The third objection is the core: if no intention is expressed, the literal meaning (hibah) should prevail.
3
Examine the possible resolutions
Consider the multiple resolutions cited from various authorities: (a) words are literal for tamlik al-ayn and metaphorical for tamlik al-manafi', so the phrase is interpreted as 'idha lam yurid al-hibata wa arada bihi al-ariyata'; (b) words are metaphorical for tamlik al-ayn, so the phrase is emphatic; (c) both meanings are literal, and the context of aariyah gives preference due to caution (tiyqan).
Each resolution comes from a different Hanafi source: Al-Kafi, Musta'li Sharh Nafi', Al-Mabsut, and Al-Kifayah.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
Identify which resolution is relied upon in the Hanafi school. The passage indicates the author of Hidayah inclined toward the first resolution (literal for tamlik al-ayn, metaphorical for tamlik al-manafi'), and this is supported by later authorities.
The key is that the ruling is not absolute; it depends on intention and linguistic convention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ علامہ علی نے الکافی میں صاحب ہدایہ کی عبارت "هذا العرب الى يحمل على تمليك المنافع تجوزاً" پر کئی وجوہ سے اشکال قائم کیا ہے۔ اول یہ کہ "اذالم " کے بجائے بھیا کہنا چاہئے۔ بدلیل آنکہ تعلیل میں لانھما تثنیہ لائے ہیں اس کا جواب یوں ممکن ہے کہ یہ کی تعمیر مذکور کی طرف راجع ہے۔ جیسے آیت میں ہے۔ عوان بین ذالک۔ دوم یہ کہ موصوف نے یہاں مخت اور حملت دونوں لفظوں کو تملیک عین کے لئے حقیقت اور تملیک منفعت کے لئے مجاز قرار دیا ہے اور کتاب البہیہ میں الفاظ بہ بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے ۔ وحملتك على هذا الدابة اذانوى بالحملان الهبة " اور اس کی علت یہ بیان کی ہے۔ ”لان الحمل هو الاركاب حقيقة فيكون عارية لكنه يحتمل الهبة " سوم ... یہ کہ جب دونوں لفظ تملیک عین کے لئے حقیقت ہوئے اور عدم نیت کے وقت لفظ سے حقیقت ہی مراد ہوتی ہے تو عدم ارادہ ہبہ کے وقت تملیک منفعت پر محمول نہیں کرنا چاہئے بلکہ ہبہ پرمحمول ہونا چاہئے۔ پھر موصوف نے مستعلی شرح نافع سے نقل کیا ہے کہ یہ بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ دونوں لفظ تملیک عین کے حقیقت اور تملیک منفعت کے لئے مجاز ہوں ۔ کتاب العاریہ میں صاحب ہدایہ کا میلان اسی طرف ہے۔ اس صورت میں تقدیر عبادت یوں ہے ۔ اذالم يرد الهبة وارادبه العارية اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ تملیک عین کے لئے مجاز ہوں۔ فخر الاسلام نے مبسوط میں اور صاحب ہدایہ نے کتاب الہبہ میں اسی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ اس صورت میں اذالم ير دبه الهبة برائے تاکید ہوگا۔ اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ دونوں لفظوں کے لئے ہر دو معنی حقیقی ہوں اور ان میں ایک کو ترجیح اس لئے ہو کہ وہ کافی الامرین ہے تو بوجہ تیقن اسی پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ (کفایه )
Warning: Allamah Ali in Al-Kafi raised objections on multiple grounds against the author of Hidayah's statement "this word is carried upon tamlik al-manafi' figuratively". First: Instead of 'idha lam' it should be 'bah' or similar because the reasoning uses the dual 'lahuma'. The answer may be that the pronoun refers back to what was mentioned, like in the verse 'awwan bayna dhalik'. Second: He (the author) made both 'manah'tu' and 'hamaltu' literal for tamlik al-ayn and metaphorical for tamlik al-manafi', while in Al-Bahiyyah it is said: 'And hamaltuka 'ala hadhihi al-dabbati if he intends hibah by the mounting', and its reason is stated: 'Because al-haml (mounting) is literal for riding, so it is aariyah, but it may bear hibah.' Third: When both words are literal for tamlik al-ayn, and when there is no intention the literal meaning is intended, then when hibah is not intended, they should not be carried upon tamlik al-manafi' but upon hibah. Then he quoted from Musta'li Sharh Nafi' that it is possible that both words are literal for tamlik al-ayn and metaphorical for tamlik al-manafi'. In the Book of Aariyah, the author of Hidayah inclines towards this. In that case, the phrase is 'idha lam yurid al-hibata wa arada bihi al-ariyata'. And there is also the possibility that they are metaphorical for tamlik al-ayn. Fakhr al-Islam in Al-Mabsut and the author of Hidayah in the Book of Hibah indicated this. In that case, 'idha lam yurid bihi al-hibata' is for emphasis. And there is also the possibility that both words have both meanings as literal, and one is preferred because it is the more cautious, so it is carried upon it due to certainty. (Al-Kifayah)
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (tanbih) from Allamah Ali in Al-Kafi objecting to the Hidayah's treatment of the words 'manah'tuka' and 'hamaltuka'. The author of Hidayah stated that when hibah is not intended, these words are carried upon tamlik al-manafi' figuratively. Allamah Ali raises three objections: First, the phrasing should use a dual pronoun, but the answer is that the pronoun refers back to the two words. Second, there is inconsistency with Al-Bahiyyah where 'hamaltuka' is considered aariyah but may bear hibah. Third, if the words are literal for tamlik al-ayn, then without intention of hibah they should be carried upon hibah (transfer of ownership) rather than usufruct. The commentary then provides multiple resolutions from various sources, including that the words may be metaphorical for tamlik al-ayn or that both meanings are literal and the context of aariyah gives preference. This demonstrates the complex linguistic analysis in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
تنبیہ (tanbih): A warning or critical note pointing out an issue in the text.
حمل (haml): The act of interpreting a word in a particular meaning.
حقیقت (haqiqah): Literal meaning of a word.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical meaning of a word.
تملیک عین (tamlik al-ayn): Transfer of ownership of the specific object (hibah).
تملیک منفعت (tamlik al-manafi'): Transfer of the benefit/usufruct of an object (aariyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary consequence of Allamah Ali's third objection?
A) The words must be interpreted as literal for tamlik al-ayn, so the transaction is hibah.
B) The words are always ambiguous and require a judge to decide.
C) The Hidayah's view is invalidated entirely.
D) The words should be understood as ariyah based on caution.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of 'manah'tuka' and 'hamaltuka' is not settled; Hanafi scholars debate whether the default is hibah or aariyah, with the relied-upon position being aariyah when no intention is expressed.

Valid Phrases for Aariyah: Akhdhamtuka, Sukna, 'Umra
Explains valid phrases for aariyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify phrases that create a valid aariyah and explain why each indicates usufruct, not ownership.

Core Idea
Phrases granting usufruct without ownership create aariyah; the key is transfer of manfa'ah not 'ayn.

Aariyah is a loan of benefit without transfer of ownership. This passage clarifies three common phrases—'akhdamtuka', 'dari laka sukna', and 'umra sukna'—that validly create aariyah. Each phrase is analyzed to show that it indicates permission to use the usufruct, not ownership of the substance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase
Read the Arabic phrase used in the aariyah contract. The passage discusses three specific phrases.
2
Analyze the legal effect of the phrase
Determine whether the phrase grants ownership of the substance or merely permission to use the usufruct. Key: does it transfer the 'ayn or just the manfa'ah?
3
Explain why it is aariyah
For each phrase, state why it creates aariyah: either because it is a permission for service (istikhdam), or because the word 'sukna' decisively indicates usufruct, or because the life grant is interpreted as a transfer of usufruct by the accompanying word 'sukna'.
4
Distinguish from other contracts
Contrast with hibah (gift) where ownership of the substance is transferred. Note that the Hanafi school interprets ambiguous phrases in favor of aariyah when only usufruct is intended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله اخدمتك ... الخ اخدمتك عبدی کہنے سے بھی عاریت ہوگی۔ کیونکہ یہ اجازت استخدام ہے۔ تملیک نہیں ہے۔ داری لک سکنی سے بھی عاریت ہوگی۔ کیونکہ لفظ سکنی منفعت میں محکم ہے تو لک کے لام کو تملیک منافع پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ اس کا محتمل ہے۔ قوله عمری سکنی ..... الخ داری لک عمری سکئی بھی عاریت ہے کیونکہ اپنے گھر کی سکونت اس کے لئے مدت عمر کر دی۔ کیونکہ سکنی کہنا لک کی تفسیر ہے۔ اسلئے کہ یہ جیسے ہیہ کو مشتمل ہے ایسے ہی تملیک منافع کلمہ یعنی سکنی کی دلالت سے اسی معنی پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔
His saying 'akhdamtuka' etc.: 'akhdamtuka 'abdi' (I gave you my slave for service) also makes aariyah valid, because it is permission for service (istikhdam), not tamlik. 'Dari laka sukna' (my house is for you to dwell in) also makes aariyah valid, because the word 'sukna' is decisive (muhkam) in [the meaning of] usufruct, so the lam of 'laka' is carried upon tamlik al-manafi', because it may bear it. His saying ''umra sukna' etc.: 'dari laka 'umra sukna' (my house is for you as a life grant of dwelling) is also aariyah, because he made the dwelling in his house for him for the duration of his life. Because saying 'sukna' is an interpretation of 'laka', because just as it contains hibah, similarly by the indication of the word 'sukna' which is a term for tamlik al-manafi', it is carried upon that meaning.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage continues explaining other valid phrases for aariyah. 'Akhdamtuka 'abdi' (I gave you my slave for service) is aariyah because it grants permission to use the slave's service, not ownership of the slave. 'Dari laka sukna' (my house is for you to dwell in) is aariyah because 'sukna' (dwelling) clearly indicates usufruct, so the particle 'laka' is interpreted as transferring the usufruct. ''Umra sukna' (life grant of dwelling) is a form of aariyah where the lender gives the house for the borrower's lifetime; the word 'sukna' clarifies that it is a transfer of usufruct, not ownership.

Key Terms
اخدمتک (akhdamtuka): The phrase 'I gave you for service', indicating permission to use a slave's services.
سکنی (sukna): Dwelling; a term for the usufruct of a house.
عمری ('umra): A life grant; giving the usufruct of a property for the recipient's lifetime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is 'dari laka sukna' considered a valid aariyah?
A) Because 'laka' indicates ownership of the house.
B) Because 'sukna' is a term for usufruct, so 'laka' is interpreted as transfer of usufruct.
C) Because it implies a sale.
D) Because the word 'dari' alone is enough.

Key Takeaway
Phrases granting usufruct without ownership—like 'akhdamtuka', 'dari laka sukna', and 'umra sukna'—create a valid aariyah contract.

Lender's Right to Revoke Aariyah at Any Time
States the lender's right to revoke aariyah at any time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on revoking aariyah and explain the proofs from hadith and gradual ownership of usufruct.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, aariyah is non-binding: the lender may revoke at any time, even if a term was set.

This passage from Al-Hidayah confirms that the lender of an item (mu'ir) may revoke the loan (aariyah) whenever he wishes. This applies whether the loan was given without a time limit or for a specified duration. The key question is whether specifying a term makes the loan binding like a lease (ijarah). The Hanafi school holds it does not, relying on a hadith and a rational argument about the gradual acquisition of usufruct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal act being ruled upon? (aariyah – loan for use). What is the ruling regarding revocation? The lender can revoke at any time.
The ruling covers both absolute and time-bound loans.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The passage cites the hadith 'al-minhatu mardudah' (the gift is returned) as a proof. Also mentions a rational argument based on gradual ownership of usufruct.
Hadith is from multiple narrators; considered ahad but accepted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith indicates that a gift (including aariyah) is returnable, implying the lender can take it back. The rational proof: usufruct is owned moment by moment; uncreated usufruct has not been possessed, so the lender can revoke before possession.
This distinguishes aariyah from ijarah, where usufruct is purchased and binding.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Imam Malik
Imam Malik does not permit revocation before the term in time-bound aariyah, treating it like ijarah. The Hanafis differ.
The practical consequence: in Hanafi, the borrower has no guarantee of the full term; in Maliki, the borrower is secure.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi view as the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) based on the hadith and the nature of the contract.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و للمعيران يرجع مغیر جب چاہے اپنی چیز واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ عاریت مطلقہ ہو یا موقته بدليل حديث لمنحته (ابوداود ترندی ابن حبان طبراني عن ابي امامه بذار عن ابن عمر بن عدي عن ابن اباس عطبراني عن انس) مردودة۔ نیز اس لئے بھی کہ منافع جس قدر پیدا ہوتے جائیں۔ اسی حساب سے تھوڑے تھوڑے ملک میں آتے ہیں تو جو منافع ابھی وجود میں نہیں آئے ان کے ساتھ تملیک کا قبضہ متصل نہیں ہوا اور قبضہ سے پہلے رجوع کرنا صحیح ہے۔ البتہ امام مالک یہاں اعادہ موقتہ میں قبل از وقت رجوع کرنا جائز نہیں - فيكون حكمها عنده كالاجارة
His saying 'and the lender has the right to reclaim': The lender may take back his item whenever he wishes. Whether the aariyah is absolute or time-bound, based on the hadith 'al-minhatu mardudah' (Abu Dawood, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani from Abu Umama... from Ibn 'Abbas, al-Tabarani from Anas). And also because usufruct comes into ownership gradually as they occur; the usufruct that have not yet come into existence have not been connected to possession, and revoking before possession is valid. However, Imam Malik does not permit revocation before the term in a time-limited loan; in his view it is like ijarah (binding lease).
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage reaffirms a key Hanafi ruling: the mu'ir (lender) may revoke the aariyah at any time, whether the loan was given for an indefinite period (mutlaqah) or for a specified time (muwaqqatah). The proof is the hadith: 'al-minhatu mardudah' (the gift is returned) and the well-known hadith 'al-ariyatu mu'adah' (the loan is repaid). The rational proof is that usufruct is owned moment by moment; for usufruct not yet created, possession has not been taken, so the lender can revoke. This differs from ijarah, which is binding. Imam Malik holds that if a time is specified, the lender cannot revoke early, treating it like a lease.

Key Terms
عاریت مطلقہ (aariyah mutlaqah): An absolute loan without any specified time limit.
عاریت موقته (aariyah muwaqqatah): A loan for a specified period.
رجوع (ruju'): Revocation; taking back the lent item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on revoking a time-bound aariyah?
A) The lender cannot revoke before the term ends.
B) The lender may revoke at any time, even before the term ends.
C) Revocation is only allowed if the borrower agrees.
D) The lender can only revoke if the item is perishable.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, aariyah is always revocable by the lender, even if a time limit is set, because the contract is non-binding.
